Street Fight Between German Extremists

Sixty-Five Seriously Injured

Reuters, Berlin, 14th - The National Socialist Party and the Communist Party engaged in a street fight here tonight, resulting in sixty-five serious injuries. Initially, the leaders of the two parties gave speeches at a sports field, with about 20,000 listeners. Unexpectedly, rioters rushed in and began to beat people, causing chaos. Many people fell to the ground and were trampled. The police used their batons in the hope of restoring order, but the streets were not cleared until several hours later.

Rumor of Joint Anglo-American Movement to Cease Warship Construction

National News Agency, Washington, 14th - Today, the Associated Press received information from reliable sources that British politicians have repeatedly suggested that Britain and the United States jointly launch a movement to abolish battleships. The presentation of this proposal is related to Anglo-American cooperation in ensuring the success of the disarmament conference. The abolition of battleships was also an important issue at the 1930 London Naval Conference, but it failed to progress due to widespread opposition. Therefore, Britain has proposed it again today, hoping that it can be realized at the disarmament conference next spring. At present, the world is paying more and more attention to disarmament, and many believe that once the burden of world armaments is reduced, economic recovery can be expected to be faster. Therefore, Senator Borah has proposed a five-year suspension of warship construction. Foreign Minister Grandi also proposed at the League of Nations to suspend warship construction temporarily before the disarmament conference next spring. When U.S. Secretary of State Stimson traveled to Europe recently, he also had detailed discussions on disarmament. It is expected that Britain and the United States will definitely consult with each other frequently this winter, hoping to reach a consensus on the battleship issue first.

Soviet Air Force Chief Inspector Dies in Accident

National News Agency, Moscow, 14th - Soviet Air Force Chief Inspector Mikhailop and his pilot Bisalunko died in an accident while inspecting somewhere. Rumors say it was caused by assassination.

Hurricane Hits Mexico

National News Agency, Miami, 14th - A hurricane swept across the east and west coasts of Mexico today. United Airlines received a radio message stating that the Mexican territory of Sopus, 150 miles north of British Honduras's Peleez, experienced a major hurricane last night, and the damage is incalculable. The Associated Press also received a message from Mexico City that a severe hurricane blew through the Lower California Peninsula on Sunday. However, news from the disaster area is scarce, only stating that the damage is extremely severe. The authorities are currently working to restore transportation in hopes of receiving more detailed information.

Arson Attack on Seville University's Chemistry Laboratory

Valuable Books Burned to Ashes

National News Agency, Madrid, 15th - The drug chemistry laboratory in a branch of Seville University, which housed many valuable books and specimens, was completely destroyed by fire early this morning, causing a loss of 2 million Spanish pesos. The authorities suspect arson and have arrested several unemployed workers.

Two Suspects Arrested in Budapest Train Bombing

Reuters, Budapest, 14th - In connection with the bombing of a railway bridge near Budapest on Saturday and Sunday, which caused a passenger train to plunge into a ravine and killed and injured many people, it has now been learned that 27 people died and more than 50 were injured. The authorities have arrested two suspects, one posing as a railway engineer and the other a Budapest student. The police detained them because they photographed the broken bridge, which was deemed suspicious. It is suspected that this incident was committed by the Communist Party.

Public Telegrams

Liu Zhenhua et al. Telegram: To all newspaper offices: We have just read Commander-in-Chief Chiang's telegram, urging the cessation of internal warfare, the suppression of bandits, and disaster relief. His words were earnest and moving. At this critical moment of internal and external troubles, when survival is at stake, how should all citizens arouse their conscience and reverse the disastrous situation? Yet a few reactionary elements in Guangdong and Guangxi are gloating over the disaster, acting perversely, and are willing to sacrifice the Party and the nation to achieve their own ends. We are deeply angered by the frequent reports of alarms. In recent days, Vice Commander Zhang and other gentlemen have sent telegrams in response, strongly defending peace, with righteous words and deep admiration. We will inspire our officers and soldiers to follow his lead, with common hatred and unwavering commitment. We respectfully submit our sincere feelings, hoping for your understanding. Liu Zhenhua, Liu Maoen, Ruan Xun, Xu Pengyun, Wu Tinglin, Xing Qingzhong, Yang Tianmin, Liu Huixin, Yao Banchen, Ma Qizhen, respectfully and earnestly.

Yantai Telegram: To all newspaper offices and all elders and brothers across the country: This year's torrential rains have caused disasters, and floods have inundated the land. The disaster areas are almost all over the country, and the land is about to sink. Homes have been destroyed, and refugees fill the fields. We are deeply saddened by the suffering of the people. On the 8th of this month, we launched the Jiaodong All Sectors National Flood Disaster Relief Association in Yantai, sending telegrams to appeal on behalf of the disaster victims. However, the disaster-stricken people are crying out for food, and disaster relief is like fighting a fire. Without raising emergency funds, nothing can be accomplished. The National Government has issued a clear order that civil servants donate their salaries to help disaster relief, and there are already regulations. Friendly countries are enthusiastically providing assistance, showing particular compassion. We, Zhennian, are honored to serve in the military, and we have a deep connection with our compatriots. It is our responsibility to save the people, and we have no other choice. We should do our best to promote this initiative to facilitate progress. Now, the officers and soldiers of this division are willing to donate what they can from their August salaries, totaling 15,000 yuan, all for disaster relief. The finances of this division are very tight, and we are unable to take care of ourselves. However, compared to the helpless disaster victims, our situation seems better. Although a cup of water cannot put out a cartload of fire, we must make every effort to provide what little we can to help. We hope that kind-hearted people will rise up, generously contribute, and jointly relieve the disaster. We await your kind instruction. Liu Zhennian, Commander of the 21st Division of the Army; He Yisan, Deputy Commander; Han Xun, Chief of Staff; Zhao Zhenqi, Liang Lizhu, Zhang Luanji, and other brigade commanders, along with all officers and soldiers, respectfully.

Important News

39th Session of the Executive Yuan's National Affairs Meeting

Allocate Funds to Relieve Distressed Overseas Chinese in Mexico

Draft Postal Law Submitted to the National Government

Appoint Liu Fu Concurrently as Civil Affairs Commissioner of Anhui

The Executive Yuan held its 39th National Affairs Meeting on the 15th. Attendees: Song Ziwen, Wang Boqun, Liu Ruiheng, Wang Zhengting, Lian Shenghai. In attendance: Chen Yi, Chen Shaokuan, Wang Zhijue, Zheng Hongnian, Chen Bulei, Zhang Wohua. Secretary-General: Lü Bichou. Director of Political Affairs: Xu Jingzhi. Chairman: Song Ziwen. The following items were discussed: (1) The joint submission of the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Military Affairs regarding the request from He Chengjun, Director of the Wuhan Garrison Headquarters, to review the petition of Gao Jipu, former Magistrate of Mianyang County, stating that county magistrates who lead teams to suppress bandits during the period of "cleansing the countryside and suppressing bandits" should be given military treatment or assigned military positions, with attached proposed measures, requesting instructions, which was reviewed. The discussion held that county magistrates have a duty to guard the soil, and should go to the scene when there is an emergency in the county. They have the power to command public security police, serve as the head of the defense corps, and concurrently serve as the director of the rural cleansing bureau in the rural cleansing area. The responsibilities are clear, and there is no need to give them a military title. As for the trial of bandit cases, it should be handled separately in accordance with the provisions of Article 16 of the Rural Cleansing Regulations and Article 7 of the Emergency Punishment Law for Endangering the Republic of China, and there is no need to give them the title of military judge. If the anti-bandit troops violate military orders, it should be reported to the respective levels of commanders for clarification of responsibilities. There is no need to set separate regulations. The provision that the organization of teams must be reported to the high-level military authorities for record is feasible. The resolution was to approve the Ministry's proposal for implementation. (2) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs reported that the situation of discrimination against Chinese in Mexico has been reported in the past, and Ambassador Xiong has been repeatedly instructed to earnestly negotiate. However, due to discrimination, the number of bankrupt and unemployed overseas Chinese is increasing daily, and funds for dismissal and relief are urgently needed. It is proposed to first order the Ministry of Finance to allocate 50,000 yuan to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for remittance to Ambassador Xiong for economical use, and to make further requests after assessing the situation. The resolution was to approve the request. (3) The Ministry of Communications reported that the Ministry has selected regulations from various countries, taken into account the situation in this country, and drafted a postal law of 55 articles, which is hereby submitted for review and transfer to the Legislative Yuan for review. The resolution was to submit the report to the National Government. (4) It was resolved that Zhu Xi, Member of the Anhui Provincial Government and concurrently Civil Affairs Commissioner, be permitted to resign from the concurrent position of Commissioner due to illness, and that the vacant position be filled by Liu Fu, Member of the Provincial Government.

Temporary Martial Law Declared in Changsha

Changsha Correspondence: Since the Yue-Gui armies launched a large-scale invasion of Hunan, the provincial authorities and the central army have been actively deploying defenses. Although the defenses in southern Hunan are extremely solid, the security of the rear areas still requires careful maintenance. As the provincial capital is a crucial base, all efforts should be made to ensure its security. Hu Da, the Garrison Commander of the provincial capital, acting upon the orders of the Fourth Route Army Headquarters, declared temporary martial law in the provincial capital yesterday (the 12th), and convened a security meeting with the heads of various agencies related to security. Those present included Zhang Tiexiang, representative of the Fourth Route Army Headquarters; Peng Zhuo, Chief of the Public Security Bureau; Liu Zeyuan, Deng Duguang, Xiao Zhaoxiong, and Li Zhenchu, Chiefs of various police stations; Li Huaqing, Commander of the Water Police Brigade; Tang Youyue, Magistrate of Changsha County; Zhu Bangji, Commander of the Security Regiment; Yang Zhaojun, Commander of the Volunteer Corps; Wang Yu and Li Xianglin, Commanders of the Garrison Regiment, and more than twenty other people. Hu Da presided over the meeting, and after lengthy discussions, the following resolutions were made: (1) Theaters, hotels, tea houses, restaurants, and the singing and dancing in all households, as well as entertainment activities that produce noise, and the setting off of firecrackers by citizens, will be temporarily prohibited from 10:00 PM every day; (2) The entire city will be divided into eight alert zones, with alert troops on patrol from 8:00 PM to 6:00 AM the next morning; (3) Special checkpoints may be set up in important locations in the provincial capital, starting from 12:00 midnight, and sentries will conduct checks on anyone who looks suspicious. If they are soldiers, their identification must be checked, and their passwords must be asked in a low voice. The passwords will not be called out unless absolutely necessary, and traffic will not be disrupted (special regulations will be made separately for special martial law periods, and passes will be issued by the police department); (4) Water traffic will be cut off from 9:00 PM to dawn the next day; (5) Night vendors will be issued permits by the Municipal Public Security Bureau based on household registration. Those without permits will be prohibited from operating; (6) Shops and households in the city will be responsible for reporting to the local group leader, who will then report to the police station, any guests lodging with them on a daily basis, and those who violate this will be detained for investigation; (7) The holding of processions to welcome gods will be strictly prohibited; (8) The Provincial Government, the Fourth Route Army Headquarters, the Anti-Opium Suppression Headquarters, the airfield, the armory, the old prison of Sijin Bay, the Changsha East Railway Station, and the Chairman's residence will all be guarded by the Fourth Company of the Special Service Regiment of the Headquarters; (9) Retired soldiers and wounded soldiers will be strictly checked and managed by the Garrison Department and the Public Security Bureau, each sending a member to work with various hospitals. The above measures will be implemented immediately, and a public notice is issued as follows: "Regarding the declaration of martial law, we received an order from Commander-in-Chief He: 1. As the Yue-Gui rebels are attempting to invade Hunan and disrupt the overall situation, troops have been dispatched to block them, and it will not be difficult to wipe them out in one fell swoop. However, the provincial capital is the political center, and local security is extremely important. At a time when bandits are rampant and hidden dangers are a concern, strict precautions must be taken to eliminate these dangers. From August 12th, temporary martial law is declared in and around the provincial capital, including the suburbs. 2. During the period of martial law, all troops stationed in the provincial capital, including allied forces, as well as the water and land police, the Changsha Security Regiment, and the Volunteer Corps, will be under the command and dispatch of the Provincial Capital Garrison Headquarters. The county government will be under its control to unify authority. 3. The martial law regulations have been formulated by this Headquarters and are being issued accordingly. In addition to issuing separate orders for the above three items, they must be strictly observed and widely publicized. This order is issued in addition to a copy of the Provincial Capital Temporary Martial Law Regulations, etc. Upon receipt of this order, it is hereby announced for the information of all residents inside and outside the city and its suburbs. Everyone should maintain their livelihoods and not stray onto the wrong path. If there are evildoers who spread rumors to confuse the public and attempt to disrupt security, they will be dealt with by military law once discovered. Everyone must abide by this." The Provincial Capital Temporary Martial Law Regulations are listed on the left: 1. The area within the city and suburbs of the provincial capital, and within key fortresses in the vicinity, is the martial law zone. 2. During the period of martial law, assemblies, organizations, strikes, and market closures deemed to impede military secrets, as well as reactionary propaganda slogans in newspapers, magazines, books, must be suppressed. For military supplies, their export may be prohibited if necessary. 3. Confiscation may occur of privately owned firearms, ammunition, weapons, fire-starting tools, and other dangerous items if necessary. 4. Mail and telegrams will be inspected. 5. Incoming and outgoing ships, vehicles, and other items will be inspected. Water and land traffic may be stopped when necessary. 6. The local militias and other groups will be supervised and guided. If there is any illegal behavior that harms military operations, it may be suppressed, or they may be ordered to surrender their weapons and disband. 7. Residents lodging in the martial law zone may be ordered to leave if necessary. 8. Day or night in the martial law zone, door-to-door inspections or spot checks may be carried out when necessary. Special attention should be paid to places where refugees gather, and they should be monitored. The Provincial Capital Garrison Headquarters will temporarily formulate measures for the aforementioned door-to-door inspections, spot checks, and refugee monitoring, considering the circumstances. 9. The performances in theaters may be suspended, and hotels, brothels, tea houses, restaurants, and other entertainment venues will be strictly inspected to prevent the concealment of criminals." (September 13th)

News from Jiangxi Regarding the Yue-Gui Armies' Invasion of Hunan

A Statement Issued by the Political Training Department of the Headquarters

Nanchang Correspondence: The invasion of Hunan by the Yue-Gui armies has become a reality. According to a certain important person in the Political Training Department of the Headquarters, the details are as follows: (Reporter asks) The news of the Yue-Gui armies sending troops is rampant. Can you shed some light on this? (The important person answers) The Yue-Gui armies are indeed eager to invade Hunan and Jiangxi, incorporating bandits such as Yan Renyi, Hu Fengzhang, and Chen Tiejian on the border of Hunan and Guangdong, and giving them names such as Newly Organized Division and Independent Brigade. According to reports, these groups have already invaded Yizhang and Chen counties. As for the Yue-Gui armies, they are still at the border between Guangdong, Guangxi, and Hunan, and have not actually invaded Hunan. The long-rumored northern offensive, when it comes to changing the stones, is difficult to realize. At this time, it is probably still a bluff, and it will soon subside. (Question) If the Yue-Gui armies do invade Hunan in the future, will the central government launch a punitive expedition? (Answer) The strength of the Yue-Gui armies: the Eighth Route Army of Guangdong has only 40,000 men, and Zhang Gui has only over 10,000 men. After deducting those who stay behind, they cannot send more than 30,000 men. After the rebellion, although they recruited new soldiers, their training is not sophisticated and they are difficult to use. As for the foreign weapons they purchased, they have been detained by the central government in Shanghai. Having soldiers without weapons is also futile. Moreover, launching a long-distance attack is a taboo in military strategy. Hunan's He has 50,000 men, which is more than enough to put down the rebellion. The central government has no need to send troops. At present, the floods are severe, so Commander-in-Chief Dong issued a telegram advocating peace, and will probably not issue a punitive order immediately. (Question) Will the Hunan issue affect the future of bandit suppression? (Answer) The remaining bandits will definitely want to take this opportunity to rekindle their dying embers. However, the central government weighs the priorities, and suppressing bandits is more urgent than suppressing rebels. Therefore, the 19th Route Army and Chiang's division are attacking bandits in the northeast of Xingguo, and the 18th Army and Wei's division are searching and suppressing in the southwest of Ningdu. The remaining Sun Lu and Shangguan's armies, Zhou Zhao, Li, and Mao's divisions are all clearing up in their original locations and have not been transferred. Even the 1st Division of Hu Zongnan's troops is still in Zhangshu and the Huaping area, twenty miles to the south, as a reserve force for bandit suppression. Nanchang to Zhangshu, can be reached in a few hours. It does not hurt to conduct an investigation, and you will know the facts. If the remaining bandits do take the opportunity to move, their suppression will be even faster. (Question) Then does the central government have any deployments between Hunan and Hubei? (Answer) Gu Zhutong has arrived in Wuhan, and he will definitely have some deployments for the Wuhan-Yue area, but it is a military secret and cannot be disclosed. (Question) Can we hear about the current situation in southern Hunan? (Answer) According to reports, Yizhang was extorted 36,000 yuan by Chen and Yan's troops, and Chen County was extorted 52,000 yuan. Various supplies are not included. Rape and looting are no different from the Red bandits, etc.

Recent Situation of Disaster Relief Work in Hubei Province

The Relief Association Telegraphed the General Association to Allocate Funds

Relief Teams Have Departed for Various Counties One After Another

Hankou Correspondence: Since the establishment of the Hubei Provincial Relief Association, it has been in close contact with the Emergency Relief Association. The first step of disaster relief work in Wuhan and various counties has been carried out. Various relief teams have also set off on different routes. However, the river water has not receded slightly for days, and the people's suffering has not been immediately relieved. If the relief funds are not continued, it is feared that they will still become starving people. The Relief Association is very concerned about this and has telegraphed the General Association to quickly allocate huge sums of money for assistance to avoid interruption, while simultaneously seeking ways to maintain the people's problems of clothing, food, shelter, and transportation. The Emergency Relief Association, the Provincial Government, and the Garrison Department are also working together. The situation in various parties is recorded separately as follows:

Telegraphed the General Association to Quickly Allocate Huge Sums of Money. The disaster area in Hubei Province is vast, and there are many disaster victims. In Wuhan alone, there are more than 400,000 disaster victims. Providing clothing and porridge requires at least 400,000 yuan per day. There are a total of 10 million disaster victims in various counties. Just in terms of food rations, each person needs 50 cents per day, which requires 500,000 yuan. The current 170,000 yuan relief funds issued by the National Government and the relief funds remitted from various parties total only more than 1 million yuan, which is only enough for two days of needs. The situation of exhaustion can be imagined. The Relief Association specifically telegraphed the Chairman of the General Association, Song Ziwen, on the 10th, requesting that the relief funds received be fully allocated and remitted to relieve the urgent need. Wen Yun, "Respectfully to Chairman Song Ziwen of Shanghai, I have received your Jia telegram and will handle the allocation of health funds accordingly. However, the use of US dollar donations is limited to the corner of Hankou. The vast areas outside the county urgently need relief, and the branch has no ability to cope. I have already clearly stated in your Jia telegram that I sincerely request that the relief funds received be fully allocated and remitted to relieve the urgent need. Respectfully, the Hubei Branch Executive Committee." The association also purchased 10,000 shi of rice in Jiangxi and 30,000 shi of rice in Anhui, but the funds were not available. They telegraphed the General Association again, saying, "Hubei Province needs rice after the disaster. Minister He of Jiangxi has agreed to purchase 10,000 shi of relief rice on behalf of the province, requiring 85,000 yuan. Another 30,000 shi of rice was purchased in Anhui Province, and personnel need to be sent immediately with funds to escort it to Hankou. However, the rice funds are not available. Please allocate 400,000 yuan for application first."

Intensified Epidemic Prevention in Refugee Shelters. There were originally many refugee shelters in Wuhan, such as the Charity Association, New Market, Ewo Godown, Baolin Godown, Longevity Palace, Taiping Guild Hall, Changsha Guild Hall, Tiancheng Cowhide Warehouse, Emperor Lord Palace, St. Joseph's Girls' School, Tongyi Association on the upper section of the Dike Street, Qianrentang in Tianbao Lane, Nancheng Public Office, and Xinhua Company in Hankou; Hongshan, Snake Mountain, Phoenix Mountain, Luojia Mountain, Wuhan University, Wenhua Middle School, Art College, Police Academy, and the 1st, 2nd, 3rd, and 9th Middle Schools in Wuchang; and Guishan, Heshan, Meizishan, and Guiyuan Temple in Hanyang. All of them have set up shelters to accommodate refugees. However, the number of people is too large and cannot be fully accommodated. In order to facilitate relief and management, the authorities have decided to accommodate refugees exclusively in Hongshan and Luojia Mountain. Reed sheds are now being built and are scheduled to be completed before the 16th. In terms of epidemic prevention, the Central Health and Epidemic Prevention Team and the provincial and municipal hospitals and the Shanghai Red Cross Society are carrying out rescue operations in different ways. Few refugees have died. However, recently, a mixed cholera and typhoid fever has been discovered in the Heshan area, and more than 10,000 people have been infected. The situation is very critical. The office of the Central Health and Epidemic Prevention Team stationed in Wuhan and the Shanghai Red Cross Society have gone to administer injections.

Bridge Construction is Not Yet Perfect. During the deep water in Hankou, the city's traffic relied entirely on boats, and the cost of hiring them was quite high. Wealthy families could still support it, but the poor did not dare to ask. When the water receded slightly and the Relief Association was established, it was decided to build temporary bridges throughout the city, divided into five main lines. The construction was completed in three days. However, due to the hasty construction, there are still imperfections, such as the bridge body being too narrow, making it difficult to pass; the board frame being not strong, leading to frequent overturning; and the bridge line being too short, so that except for important streets, people still have to wade through the water. Regarding the first and second points, the Public Security Bureau has sent a letter to the association to improve them. The citizens' request to extend the bridge line is even more urgent. It is heard that the association respects public opinion and has instructed Zhao Huanzhang, who is responsible for the project, to handle it separately. Yu Tianbi, who was sent by the Shanghai Social Bureau to work, also made suggestions on maintaining the traffic on the wooden bridge: First, people must go left and right and not walk arbitrarily to hinder traffic. Second, it is forbidden to carry heavy objects or carriers to and from the bridges to avoid danger. The association has also kept this for reference.

Commodities at Parity Prices and Rent-Free Housing. When the flood occurred, in order to prevent unscrupulous merchants from raising prices, the headquarters specifically ordered the Chamber of Commerce to order merchants not to take the opportunity to raise the prices of daily necessities such as rice, charcoal, oil, and salt. Those who violate this will be dealt with by military law. However, as time went on, the price of goods gradually increased again, and there were situations such as using inferior goods to deceive and obtain high prices. The citizens suffered from this and could not do anything. Recently, the Garrison Headquarters learned of this and detained the unscrupulous merchants for investigation and punishment, to warn the others. On the 11th, Ye Peng, the chief of staff of the headquarters, personally went to the Chamber of Commerce to discuss with He Hengfu, the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, and convened a meeting of representatives of various merchants, explaining the pros and cons repeatedly. The whole group decided to organize a temporary committee to evaluate prices, and elected representatives of the machine rice, grain, flour, kerosene, and grocery groups as members, which was established on the same day to engage in evaluation. In addition, what the people urgently requested was the issue of rent exemption, because the citizens were miserably flooded and could not afford to pay rent even if they tried to save the dead. They have repeatedly requested the Relief Association to inform the owners to exempt the rent for three months. It is heard that the association will send a letter to the commercial owners' association to exempt all of them in order to alleviate the people's difficulties.

Restricted the Use of Relief Funds in Various Counties. The disaster area in each county is extremely wide, and the disaster victims are eagerly awaiting relief. Although relief funds from various parties have been allocated to the counties, they can only be supported for a while. The provincial government deeply worries that there are situations of misappropriation in various counties, which will hinder the relief progress. On the 11th, it specifically ordered the county magistrates to pay close attention. No matter whether the relief funds are issued by the central and local relief associations or the funds raised by the county itself, they can only be used for relief and must not be diverted to other expenses. If there is any abuse of relief funds for other purposes, it will be severely punished. (September 11th)

Wuhu Water Level Still Rising Sharply

Wuhu Correspondence: The Wuhu water level has continued to rise sharply for days, exceeding the previous record by more than a foot. The entire territory has become a large lake, and there is no day for the water to recede. The disaster is prolonged, and the problem of urgent relief is even more difficult. The 15,000 yuan relief funds allocated by the central government have been collected by Wu Xingzhou, the representative who went to the province to attend the meeting, but it is still a drop in the bucket and is not enough for distribution. At present, the trend of intercepting and robbing rice in various counties in southern Anhui is growing day by day, which is likely to incite incidents. Qian Danwu, the central disaster investigation commissioner, inspected along the way and witnessed this situation. He has specifically telegraphed the Anhui Provincial Government, requesting that measures be taken quickly to stop it in order to curb the chaos. Yesterday, the county government captured a bandit in the countryside and cut off his head, which was hung up for public display. Zhang Gongheng, a member of the National Government's Flood Relief Committee, departed from Wuhu to inspect various counties in southern Anhui. He has now completed his work and will transfer to Anqing today (the 14th) to inspect various places in central Anhui. Cui Lianggong, She Ceqin, He Wuzi, and other citizens from various counties in southern Anhui specially drafted a presentation, which was presented to Commissioner Zhang and also presented to the Provincial Relief Committee, outlining methods for disaster relief in Anhui, with the content divided into three points, excerpted as follows:

"Lianggong and others believe that it should be divided into three major periods, and the following is a detailed description (1)

The urgent relief period: In urgent relief, it seems that saving the lives of disaster victims should be the top priority. It cannot be stopped for a single day until the accumulated water recedes. The one and only standard that is considered certain during this period is to weigh whether the disaster-stricken area has self-help capabilities, and refer to the severity of the disaster to determine. The views of Central Commissioner Yan are very correct. The disaster-stricken counties in our province account for two-thirds of the entire province. Whatever has happened in the past is irrelevant. In the future, when distributing urgent relief, apart from Wuhu, which has suffered heavy disasters and is also a place for refugees from north and south of the Yangtze River to seek food, and is also an important place for security along the Yangtze River, it should be recognized as having special circumstances. Other disaster-stricken counties should be distributed according to the meaning of urgent relief, and the distribution should be based on whether they can be distributed separately. Even if it cannot be completely fair, it seems better than relying on land area or population. This is the first period. (2) Winter relief period: Winter relief means repairing damaged dikes after the water recedes, maintaining the food and clothing of disaster victims, and ensuring that work will not be abandoned in the future. During this period, it seems that the extent of dike damage in each county should be investigated as the basis for distributing the amount of winter relief. In addition to providing relief to the elderly and weak, the proposal to replace relief with work should be discussed and handled with local authorities. This is the second period. (3) Spring relief period: Spring relief refers to the time when the green and yellow crops are not yet harvested. Without relief funds, there is no way to survive. Without seeds, there is no way to return to farming. During this period, the amount of relief funds should be distributed according to the disaster-stricken land area in each county, because the disaster-stricken land area in each county is roughly the same. The disaster victims can also be inferred from this. Other things can be ignored. This is the third period. In short, there is no good strategy for disaster relief, as ancient people have said clearly. If a certain goal is taken as a single method from beginning to end, I am afraid it will not be enough to show fairness."

Investigation of the Disaster Situation in Jiangxi Province

Poyang Disaster Area is Over a Thousand Kilometers

Page 10

Flash Floods in the Gan River and Fu River Erupt Again

The Flood Emergency Relief Association Has Been Established

Nanchang Correspondence: This year, due to the flooding of the Yangtze River and Poyang Lake in this province, 27 counties, including Nanchang, Xinjian, Jiujiang, Poyang, Duchang, and Pengze, have reported floods. Counties that have not reported include Anyi, Ji'an, and Qingjiang. Among them, the most severe floods are in Jiujiang and Poyang counties. Poyang County is located on the shore of Poyang Lake, at the outlet of the Raohe and Xinhe rivers. The terrain is low-lying. This summer and autumn, the water of the Yangtze River flowed back into the lake, and the water of the Raohe and Xinhe rivers poured into the lake. The overflowing flood caused the Poyang area to be submerged in water for the most part from the beginning of July to the present. According to Poyang County, based on custom and experience, the water will not recede until after the Mid-Autumn Festival in the lunar calendar. Regarding the disaster situation in the county, according to the results of the investigation by Zhang Qi, the disaster investigator of the Ministry of Internal Affairs, there are a total of more than 282,000 disaster victims, more than 29,000 people displaced by the disaster, more than 1,100 disaster victims who died of illness, more than 10 million in property losses, and more than 980,000 mu of flooded farmland, with an estimated reduction in crop yield of about 70%. The disaster area is 1,417 square kilometers. In addition, Zhao Liantao, the chairman of the county Chamber of Commerce, came to the province yesterday to beg for relief. According to him, the Taiping Embankment in the eastern territory collapsed on the 9th, with a gap of half a mile long, drowning more than a thousand people and collapsing more than a hundred houses. The disaster is severe and can be imagined.

In Jiujiang, the water level is now slightly lower, and the water mark is currently at 52 feet. Refugees are still being continuously accommodated, work relief is being organized, and permits for refugees to go out and beg for food have been suspended. The entire city is making every effort to carry out drainage, disaster relief, epidemic prevention, and other work. Pengze County is still in the water. Duchang, Yujiang, and other counties are still vast expanses of water in low-lying areas. The above is the disaster situation in various places in northern Jiangxi. Unexpectedly, since the beginning of this month, the weather has been cold, with continuous rain for ten days. The Gan River and Fu River also experienced flash floods. The water level in Ji'an was as high as one zhang. Low-lying areas around Xiajiang and Zhangshu were a vast expanse of water, with a water depth of more than one zhang in Wanshe and other places 30 li from the city. The Xixiang Zhiti embankment in Nanchang has already collapsed, with more than one million in losses of farmland and property. At the same time, flash floods on the Fu River caused disasters, and the late rice along the coast was completely submerged. According to news from the Water Police Bureau yesterday, the water level of the Gan River rose by three feet on the 9th and two feet on the 10th. Thatched houses in places across the river from Nanchang, such as Xinzhou and Chao Wangzhou, are about to be submerged, so they are moving away one after another. The replanted late rice in the two counties of Nanxin is in the process of flowering and fruiting, and has been declared hopeless after this flood. Moreover, in the past two days, there have been many floating corpses along the river outside Zhangwai, presumably either killed by the Red bandits or drowned by the flood. Liu Erjing and others, who were sent by the central government to investigate the floods, have taken a ship to Ji'an and other places to investigate.

The Flood Emergency Relief Association, initiated by various circles, held its inaugural meeting at the Provincial Party Headquarters on the 10th. Dozens of people were present, including Zheng Zhongwu, a member of the Provincial Party Headquarters, Xiong Yuxi, the acting chairman of the Provincial Government, and Huang Wenzhi. It was decided to elect representatives of various agencies present as members, and He Yingqin, Lu Dipin, Cao Haosen, Cheng Tianfang, and other 19 people as standing committee members. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce was used as the venue, and fundraising and disaster relief work were actively carried out. (September 10th)

The Water Outside Jiangdu City Has Not Yet Receded

Situation of Refugee Accommodation and Treatment

Current Situation of Blocking and Building and Construction Plan

Yangzhou Correspondence: After the Yunhe Dike breached, the disaster situation in a dozen or so counties north of the Yangtze River was dire. It has now been almost two weeks since the breach, but the disaster situation in Jiangdu County, such as Zhangwang Town, 25 li from the city, is still submerged in water within a 25 li radius. The shallowest point of Daijia Bridge is 5 feet deep. The water in Yuanyi No. 2 Embankment is level with the eaves. The water in Wushengzhou is over 1 zhang deep. Yesterday (the 13th), the Suzhou Relief Association's office in Yangzhou dispatched personnel such as Kong Kewei to provide relief. They took the Grand Canal out of the Guazhoukou, went east along the Yangtze River, entered Shatou, passed Huajiayao and Bagangkou, and landed at Wudai Bridge. After walking more than 3 li, they finally arrived after detouring more than 120 li. They sailed through the flooded fields in small boats and distributed relief to each household. There are an estimated 8,000 or more disaster victims. There are many other similar cases. On the 14th, those who went to the United Office of Disaster Relief Groups to beg for relief included the fifth district office and various groups in Daqiao, the sixth district office in Yiling, and the seventh district flood relief association, also sending personnel to participate and attend. On the 14th, the United Reception Office of Various Disaster Groups decided to hold regular meetings once every Monday, Wednesday, and Friday mornings at 10:00 AM, and temporary meetings would be held when necessary.

Refugee Accommodation and Treatment. Refugee shelters in Yangzhou Changsheng Temple and other places were already overcrowded. Now, the sixth refugee shelter has been established at Longqing Temple outside the West Gate, accommodating a total of 4,123 people, many of whom are suffering from dysentery, malaria, and other infectious diseases. On the 14th, Chen Peiqiu, a doctor dispatched by the Red Swastika Society to examine the patients, reported that the infectious nature was very rapid. A special commissioner carried a large number of epidemic prevention serums and invited Sun Liqing, a standing committee member of the Western Medical Association, and Xie Jiayin, Zhang Liran, and assistants such as Chen Zhaowen, to rush to Changsheng Temple and other places to administer injections, epidemic prevention needles, and surgery.

Blocking and Building Engineering and Planning. The breaches in the Shao and Gao embankments, except for the 16 breaches in the Shao Embankment that have been blocked by the Jiangdu section, the Black Fish Pond South Breach, which is currently being blocked, is scheduled to be completed on the 17th. The Hualian Pond, which is exposed and dangerous, will also be rushed to completion. Five soil transport ships that have been sealed and hired have been towed by the Runtai ship and went to work on the 14th. At the same time, large and small cables and wooden piles needed for construction are being purchased and transported for the use of blocking and building at Zhaoguan Dam, Hualian Pond, and Laisheng Temple. The temporary office of the Provincial Water Conservancy Bureau in Yangzhou has implemented the work plan decided by the Post-Disaster Engineering Committee to block and build the breaches in Gaoyou. In addition to purchasing 10,000 shi of stone in advance, it has also purchased various materials and is actively transporting them to the post office to block and build the breaches at Dangjunlou and other places, which can only be completely completed after two months.

Water Level Falling in the East and Rising in the West. As the Shaobo breach has not been blocked, the canal water flows straight down to the east, and a step has been seen to fall. According to the Shaobo report, the water mark has fallen by another two inches. However, the Jiangchao River from Guakou is topped and pushed directly into the canal outside Yangzhou City. Each tide rises by about a foot, and only drops by eight or nine, and is rising step by step every day. Fortunately, the passing hurricane was not realized.

Important Water Conservancy News from the Jiangsu Construction Bureau

Dispatching Personnel to Survey the Eastern Dam: The Eastern Dam of Gaochun's eastern border is crucial for water storage and drainage. The Construction Bureau, based on a report from the Liyang County Bureau, states that the water level difference above and below the dam is as great as 9.5 meters, making the situation extremely serious. Recently, Wang Yu was specially commissioned, along with Jiang, a member of the Civil Affairs Bureau, to conduct an on-site inspection. A telegram was received from Commissioner Wang stating that an agreement was reached with Commissioner Jiang to conduct the inspection in Gaochun County on the 15th.

Commencement of Songjiang Seawall Project: The Water Conservancy Bureau received a telegram from the head of the Jiangnan Seawall Works Office stating that he had arrived in Songjiang to make arrangements. On the 1st, he, along with Magistrate Shen, Director Sun, and local gentry, went to Jinshanwei to re-examine the dangerous condition of the seawall. The public sentiment is very urgent. Engineer Bao Zhen of the Shen Engineering Firm will be stationed at the site to take charge of the work, which will commence tomorrow. In addition to the 10,000 yuan allocated by the Songjiang County Bureau, the funds are far from sufficient. A request has been made for an additional 10,000 yuan. The bureau has already telegraphed 10,000 yuan, and Chief Engineer Pei will travel there immediately to provide guidance.

Laying a Light Railway for the Transportation of Supplies for Closing the Yun Embankment Breach: The Construction Bureau, in order to facilitate transportation for closing the breach in the Yun Embankment, deemed it necessary to lay a light railway. Yesterday, a special order was issued to the magistrates of Wuxi, Yixing, and Liyang counties, stating that the bureau is currently undertaking the project to close the breach in the Jiangbei Yun Embankment and urgently needs to transport 250 tons of light railway materials from the Jinghang Road by ship, via Liyang Nandujiang, Yixing, and Wuxi, to Gaoyou for use. Yao Jun and Hu Buren, staff members of the Highway Bureau, have been dispatched to Liyang Nandujiang to expedite transportation matters. In order to ensure speed, the county magistrates are responsible for chartering the necessary steamships and cargo ships by a specific date. The bureau will provide fuel for the steamships and freight charges for the cargo ships. In addition to dispatching the staff members to the counties for coordination, the magistrates are urged to coordinate quickly and without delay.

The Disaster Situation in Henan Province is Also Severe

The flooding in Henan Province this year has affected more than 70 counties, with Yancheng, Linying, and Xihua being the most severely affected. These three counties are located in the Shaying River basin. The Shaying River originates from Mount Tianxi and merges with the Ru River in Linru, the Hui River in Yexian, the Li River in Wuyang, the Gan River in Fangcheng, and the Guai River in Neixiang, before converging into a single stream in Yancheng. The water volume is enormous, flowing horizontally to the south-central part of Xihua. The Ying River originates from Dengfeng and, after passing through Yuxian and Xiangcheng, has already become a spectacle. In Linying, it merges with the water collected from various ponds, leading to widespread inundation. The dikes on both sides of these two rivers have been neglected for years, and the riverbeds are silted up, higher than the surrounding land. This summer and autumn, heavy rains persisted for days, causing flash floods. The rivers in the three counties merged into one, surging and overwhelming, leaving the people destitute. The Provincial Relief Committee estimates that 74 counties have been affected by the disaster in the province. Without a substantial amount of 15 million yuan this winter and spring, the starving victims will find it difficult to survive. Although the central government has dispatched personnel with funds for emergency relief, and charitable organizations from both the north and south are running around raising donations, sparing no effort, and all sectors of the military and government are also donating salaries to promote this cause, the disaster area is too vast, making universal relief difficult. Yesterday, a special telegram was sent to the business community in the province, urging them to remember the disaster victims and generously donate substantial funds for relief.

Rampant Banditry in Eastern Xuzhou

Entire Student Body of Suining County Normal School Abducted

Xuzhou Correspondence: The southeastern part of Xuzhou has long been plagued by bandits, especially the border area between Tongshan and Suining. Suining County is about 150 miles from Xuzhou. For several years, it has been disturbed by bandits from time to time. Lingchengji, 25 miles east of Suining, is a stronghold for bandits. Recently, the bandits have moved westward from Lingchengji, occupying the Daxiaoguandi Temple area, only about 20 miles from the city. The bandit leaders are Liu Rongduo, Wei San, etc., with about a thousand men. On the 11th of this month, taking advantage of the fact that Zhang Zhan Kui's Third Cavalry Division, which was stationed in Suining, had been transferred to Fengxian, leaving the city empty, the bandits seized the opportunity to lead a crowd to besiege the city. Magistrate Ni Weiqing had already gone to the provincial capital to arrange for the arrival of replacement troops. The county seat only had a police force of over a hundred men who guarded the city and kept the city gates tightly closed. The bandits failed to achieve their goals after attacking from all sides. Outside the east gate, there is a county-run normal school headed by Principal Bao Geng Guang, with about a hundred students. After looting outside the city, the bandits abducted all the students and two teachers, returning to the Lingchengji area to occupy it. Afterwards, the county government urgently telegraphed a report to the province and requested troops from the Pacification Commissioner's Office. Magistrate Ni returned from the province to Xuzhou on the 13th and immediately telegraphed Suining City to inquire about the situation and invited representatives from the party headquarters to Xuzhou to discuss the aftermath. He plans to go to the province to report again. It is reported that the bandits have released dozens of students, keeping more than ten wealthy ones for ransom. The northeast gates of Suining City are still closed. Only the west gate, which is the main road to Xuzhou, can be opened. Transportation in various districts of the county is obstructed due to banditry. As for the replacement troops, the Pacification Commissioner's Office initially dispatched Liang Guanying's 25th Route Army. Before Liang's troops arrived, there are rumors that Zhang Huatang's First Cavalry Division has been reassigned from Yaowan to the area. (14th)

Han Fuju to Inspect Eastern Shandong

Jinan Correspondence: Han Fuju, Chairman of the Shandong Provincial Government and concurrently the Chief of Clearing Countryside in Shandong and Henan, after returning from Henan, immediately began to handle the clearing of the countryside. Now the provincial bandit suppression conference has concluded, and the generals have returned to their defense areas, mobilizing troops and actively suppressing bandits according to the six designated areas. Han specially took the Jiaoji train to the Jiaodong area this afternoon (the 13th) to inspect the troops. Key figures from the party, government, and military agencies went to the station to see him off. At 5:30 PM, Han arrived at the station by car, escorted by a company of guards led by Yu Jinghuan, the chief of the General Staff's administrative section. According to Han, Ma Hong Kui's 15th Route Army was ordered to transfer to Henan, and the defenses they left behind will be taken over by Gu Liangmin's 22nd Division in the Tai'an area, and Zhan Shutang's 81st Division in the Yizhou area. "I haven't seen Zhan's troops for half a year," he said, "so I'm going to give them a lecture before they head to Linyi, Tancheng, Feixian, and Yishui. I will inspect the garrisons in the places I pass through, such as Zhoucun, Qingzhou, Changle, Weixian, Gaomi, Jiaoxian, and will also take the opportunity to inspect the politics of the various counties. I expect to be back in Jinan in four or five days." Han also invited Zhang Weicun of the Provincial Reorganization Committee to talk, telling him that since Zhan's troops are going to Yizhou, "you can send a telegram to the local authorities in advance to take care of everything (because Zhang is from Yizhou)." Zhang said that he had already sent a telegram, and then they said goodbye. Han boarded the train and left Jinan eastward at 5:45 PM. Before Han returned to the province, military affairs will be temporarily handled by Cao Fulin, the commander of the 29th Division, and political affairs will be temporarily managed by Li Shuchun, the Director of the Civil Affairs Department. (13th)

President of South Manchuria Railway Inspects Andong

Japanese Residents Petition for Establishment of Steel Plant and Railway Between Shin-Gishu and Ryongampo Andong Correspondence: The newly appointed President and Vice President of the South Manchuria Railway (SMR), Uchida and Eguchi, respectively, departed from Dalian late last month and inspected the line. They have now completed their inspections and arrived in Andong at 7:20 AM on the 8th of this month by train from Shenyang. Leaders from the Japanese community, government, commerce, and industry gathered at Andong Station to welcome them. President Uchida and Vice President Eguchi shook hands with each of those who welcomed them after disembarking from the train. They were then led to the VIP room by the stationmaster of Andong Station and Consul Mizawa to rest for a moment before meeting with influential Japanese officials and civilians to inquire about the situation. Their entourage had refreshments in another room. The entourage included Shanxi, a director; Dr. Shiba; Deputy Director of the Technical Bureau Hashi; Councilor Lin; Chief of the Agricultural Affairs Division Matsushima; Chief of the Railway Department Furu Kawa; Secretaries Matsudaira and Yagi; Clerks Itakura and Nakamura from the Document Section; and Consultants Yamai and Kenda—a total of twelve people. At the same time, Governor Kimura of Shin-Gishu and Heads of the Chamber of Commerce Tada and Kato crossed the river from Shin-Gishu to Andong and joined the Head of the Andong Chamber of Commerce and Industry, Arakawa, and three others to pay their respects. Tada and others stated that they had come to represent Japanese residents of Andong and Shin-Gishu to petition for the early realization of the establishment of a Showa Steel Plant in Shin-Gishu and to request that the SMR provide practical assistance in laying a light railway section between Shin-Gishu and Ryongampo to connect with the Gyeongui Line to facilitate transportation in Western Korea. Vice President Eguchi replied that although the two matters are urgent, they are major and cannot be determined in the shortest possible time. However, within the realm of possibility, he would do his best to assist in their realization. Eguchi also stated the SMR's future goals for new economic policies and that starting in the spring of next year, the SMR would improve education along the line. At this time, reporters from various Japanese newspapers requested interviews. Uchida gathered the reporters together and gave a brief answer because of time constraints. Then, according to the predetermined schedule, he separately conducted inspections.
