1930 Bonds Also Continued to Increase by One Yuan and Several Jiao:

Yesterday, spot bond transactions were still scarce, with only 3,000 yuan transacted throughout the day. The futures market was generally still quite good. It is estimated that over 10.06 million were transacted in the morning market, and about 4.5 million in the after-market, totaling over 15.1 million yuan. Among them, the salt tax was still the most popular, and the unified tax 20 customs share also accounted for a large amount. The trend was slightly more stable than the previous day. All parties bought at low prices, and the prices were more solid than before. Except for a rather sluggish opening in the early morning, the prices gradually rose later. As a result, the biggest increase compared to the previous day was in the salt tax for September, which reached 1.6 yuan. The October futures and the 1930 Bonds also increased by about one yuan, and others also increased by 3 or 4 jiao or so. Only the spot six Bond fell by one yuan compared to the beginning of last week.

Mediocre Situation in Cotton Yarn Market

The yarn market is flat again. Because the overseas cotton yarn situation is only inclined to go upstream, the current situation is quite prosperous, making people's hearts weaker. However, a large number of new offerings are relatively lacking, due to the floor price relationship. However, the surrounding environment is very bad, so the major shorts remain unmoved. As for the longs, their attitude is calm, so the overall trend does not deviate from a fluctuating pattern.

People's Standard Dropped Two, Three, and Four Cents: The People's Standard market opened, with the price of US cotton 3-grade yarn all dropping, and the atmosphere was relatively flat. The fine yarn price dropped by 1.2 cents. In the afternoon, it was heard that the cotton market was easing, with a looser situation, each dropping by 1, 2, 3, and 4 cents. The trading volume was estimated at 10,500 bales. It was found that Hengde sold 550 bales, Yi Da 300 bales, Shen Ji 300 bales, and Shen Xin 300 bales. Yi Yu bought 1,200 bales, Yu Da 550 bales, Tong Yu 400 bales, and Hou Feng 400 bales. The closing price is recorded on the left.

1,000 Bales of Yarn Sales: The sales of existing yarn are still good. It was found that all the gangs bought a total of 1,000 bales throughout the day. 10 bales were traded between colleagues, and the market was flat. Among the customer gangs, Tianjin bought 100 bales, Guangdong 165 bales, Shantou 105 bales, North Gang 55 bales, inland 100 bales, Sichuan 340 bales, and miscellaneous gangs 150 bales.

Cotton Market Relapses into Slump

The cotton market was flat in the morning but declined in the afternoon, with a relatively weak trend. In reality, foreign cotton prices continued to fall. Furthermore, various factories purchased large quantities of cheap American and Indian cotton, causing increasing panic among people. The market conditions deteriorated rapidly. However, due to the worsening weather in this port and the damage to cotton fields, most cotton merchants still held long positions. The global cotton situation is very pessimistic. As for speculators, they are holding their short positions firmly.

Hankou Standard Price Falls Below Four Taels Threshold

The Hankou Standard price on the exchange opened in the morning session. Although American cotton had been declining, due to poor weather, prices for all months rose slightly by five points. In the afternoon, news of large-scale foreign cotton transactions caused the market to weaken suddenly, with each price falling by 2.5 cents. The total volume of transactions was 61,300 piculs. According to investigations, Yu Chang sold 3,400 piculs, Tian Long 1,800 piculs, and Yuan De 1,800 piculs. Da Fu bought 1,100 piculs, De Ji 2,900 piculs, Ji Feng 1,400 piculs, Ming De 1,100 piculs, and Shen Chang 1,500 piculs. The closing prices are recorded below:

Foreign Cotton Yarn Plummets Universally

American Cotton Sold Off in the South

Yesterday, American cotton weakened due to a lack of major buyers, sell-offs in the South, and a downturn on Wall Street. Futures fell by 4-7 points, and spot prices fell by 5 points. British cotton futures fell by 5-6 points, while spot prices remained unchanged. Egyptian cotton spot prices remained unchanged. Indian cotton softened due to unfavorable news from Liverpool and talks by the Governor-General about increasing taxes to restore fiscal balance. Pingguoer and Oumula fell by 3 rupees, and Bai Luodan fell by 3.25 rupees. The original telegram is recorded below (dated the 14th):

Grain and Rice Market in the Lower Reaches of the River Strengthens Due to Rain

Southern Market

The supply from various groups remains low. Yesterday's market was further tightened due to the rain. Retail sales of fresh goods in urban and rural stores were still strong, while wholesale merchants were unhealthy. The demand from outside the city was good, causing the price of thick japonica and thin indica rice to rise by 2 jiao. Although there were not many foreign superior goods, transactions between the dealers and the local street were sluggish, and the market remained stable. New japonica rice was still sporadic, with normal consumption, and large fluctuations of about 2 chi were observed.

New Wharf

Yesterday, there were over 20 suppliers. River cargo customers insisted on not selling unless prices rose. Prices in inland areas such as Changshu and Yixing exceeded those in Shanghai by 6-7 jiao. Due to the cost pressures on the customers and the heavy rain, although transactions were not brisk, the market trend improved, and prices rose by 1-2 jiao. The arrival of green-tip rice remained scarce, with no demand. Glutinous rice was stable.

Foreign Rice Prices Fall and Sales Increase

Taizhou rice down 0.1 jiao, small assorted rice down 0.2 jiao.

Foreign rice arrivals surge, overseas telegrams also show slight decrease.

Yesterday, the foreign rice market unanimously declined due to the surge in arrivals and the slight decrease in overseas quotations. Foreign firms offered No. 1 Saigon rice for October delivery at only 6.7 taels, with hopes of further approval. Furthermore, rice orders for August had already arrived in succession, and orders for September would also arrive gradually. According to foreign merchants, most of the September orders, totaling over 200,000 bags, could arrive in Shanghai within the next ten days. Therefore, cargo owners and foreign firms were actively selling, and prices were willingly reduced. After the price reduction, local hoarding merchants inquired, and actual sales increased due to the cheap prices. The market became active again. However, spot prices for small-pattern rice were down by 0.2 jiao, and September contracts were down by a significant 0.1 qian. Taizhou rice and pattern rice were each down by a small amount. Approximately 5,000 bags of spot small-pattern rice were sold at prices ranging from 13 yuan to 12.75 yuan, and 200 tons for September delivery were priced at 6.2 taels. 200 bags of Mindang rice were priced at 13 yuan, and over 200 bags of Taizhou rice were priced at 12.8 yuan to 12.2 yuan, with inferior quality at 11.9 yuan. Coarse rice was priced at 11 yuan.

Wheat Market Relapses into Weakness in the Afternoon

After the opening of the wheat market yesterday, scattered merchants and inland groups bought in response to foreign wheat telegrams reporting a 0.2-0.3 increase, and prices for both near-term and far-term months rose by 0.1-0.2 points. However, the appetite of importers was limited, and brokers and large long-position holders wanted to take advantage of the rally to cash out, so the market was unable to rally. Although the volume of transactions was higher in the afternoon than in the morning, prices fell instead. The closing price for September was down 0.1 point, October was unchanged, November was down 0.1 point, December and January were unchanged, and February was up 0.1 point. Both arriving and stored wheat were available, but factory demand remained sluggish, and the market was weak. Yesterday, Huafeng Factory handled over 1,000 bags of wheat from Zhenjiang and Yangzhou.

Flour from Northern Groups Cashes Out in the Near Term

After the flour market opened yesterday, manufacturers did not sell off, and actual sales customers did not inquire. The market was unusually quiet, and transactions were scarce, a stark contrast to the prosperity of the past few months. However, the morning opening reports of increases of around 0.3 yuan attracted scattered merchants and inland customers to buy in. Inland customers paid more attention to distant months, so prices for all months rose. However, as foreign groups saw sluggish actual sales in the area, they actively cashed out near-term contracts, and the market was dragged down again. The final result was a decrease of 0.25 cents for September, unchanged for October, a decrease of 0.5 cents for November, a decrease of 0.25 cents for December, an increase of 7.5 cents for January, and an increase of 2.5 cents for February.

Wujin Autumn Cocoons Have 60% Maturity

The cocoon quality is also good... The highest cocoon price reached 80 yuan.

In the cities and villages under the jurisdiction of Wujin County, most farmers raised autumn silkworms this year. The silkworm eggs hatched well, and the weather was suitable after hatching, leading to smooth development. However, during the major molt, continuous autumn rains and cold weather affected the silkworms, resulting in white muscardine and softening diseases, causing losses of 30-40%. Early cocoons have already entered the market, and late cocoons are also ready to be spun. Overall, they have 60% maturity. Cocoon shops have been open for four days, with prices being raised and competed for. The cocoon quality is good, and the highest cocoon price has reached 80 yuan.

Piece Goods, Coarse Cloth, and Coarse Twill Sales Suddenly Surge

Due to the active distribution of clothing.

Piece goods...due to the severe flooding in various provinces, sales are cleared, reaching... Among the soft cotton cloths, light-weight coarse cloth and coarse twill are quite active, already showing signs of... Because large quantities of disaster relief funds have been collected and are being shipped out, charitable individuals who donate cotton clothing are also unusually enthusiastic. The materials for donated clothing are nothing more than coarse cloth and coarse twill, so after continuous activity in recent days, there is now a shortage. Prices have also risen one after another. 9-pound cloth is especially popular. Yesterday, Jubao Basin was priced at 4 taels and 9.5 qian, Five Fortune Cats at 5 taels and 0.5 fen, 11-pound Ren Zhong at 5 taels and 5 qian, and Three Rabbits and Three Deer at 5 taels and 6 qian. 11-pound cat-branded coarse twill also reached 5 taels and 8 qian. 12-pound Three Fish was priced at 6 taels, an increase of 0.2-0.3 qian compared to last week. 13-pound coarse cloth also showed slight firmness, with Shuang Ying at 6 taels and 7 qian, and Flying Bear at 6 taels and 5.5 qian. Among the 16-pound cloths, Hongfu from Zhentai Factory was the most stable, selling at 8 taels and 1.5 qian, and Five Cranes at 8 taels and 2 qian. Among the fine twills, Jincheng sold at 7 taels and 5.5 qian, and Balloon fine cloth at 7 taels and 5 qian. Japanese factory goods have plummeted across the board, showing a trend of irreversible decline.

Woolen Fabric Market is Excellent

The woolen fabric market has made great progress recently, with dealers actively purchasing. The weather is cool, stimulating actual sales, and retail business in stores is also suddenly booming. The silk cocoon industry is also extremely busy. Printed flannels such as Zhigong, Serge, Huashi flannel, Chocolate, and raincoat fabrics are selling extremely well, with both boxed and individual piece sales. Compared to last month's market conditions, there is much better color. The transactions for Melton, thick and thin Sea Tiger velvet, Shaorong, cotton velvet, leopard-skin mink velvet, colorful plaid overcoat fabric, printed flannels, and rotten silk flannels are also active. Most are first ticketed and settled, with staggered deadlines for clearance. A significant number are paid for in cash on the spot. Judging from the recent trend in the woolen fabric market, thick goods are better than thin goods.

Local News Two

Huangpu River Tide Rises Greatly

Bund Area Flooded

Jiujiang Road Turns Into Swamp

Yesterday's Weather, Alternating Between Cloudy and Rainy, Huangpu River Autumn Tide, Rolling In Around 1:15 PM, Rose Sharply in an Instant, Around 3 PM, the Water Was Level With the Riverbank, Causing Guangdong Road, Fuzhou Road, Hankou Road, Jiujiang Road, and the Area Bordering Sichuan Road, Due to the Lower Terrain, to Turn Into a Swamp, Jiujiang Road From the Central Bank West to the End of Jiangxi Road, Was One Foot Deep, the Water Volume Was Also Huge at the East End of the Public Works Department, So When Trolleys Passed By, Water Splashed Everywhere, Becoming a Spectacle, the Bund Park Area, Bordering the Huangpu River, Was Even More Directly Impacted, the Water Volume on Both Banks of the Suzhou Creek Was Also Almost Level With the Shoreline, the Road Behind the Fenglin Bridge Municipal Government in West Shanghai Was Also Flooded, and Pedestrians Had to Take Other Routes, Kangdi Road and Luvan Road in the French Concession, Also Due to the Lower Terrain, Sewage Surged Out of the Gutters, and There Was Water Up to an Inch Deep, Until Around 4 PM, When the Huangpu River Tide Receded, All Places Gradually Returned to Their Original State, But Rickshaws Tripled Their Profits

Two Pedestrians Wrongfully Killed by Police Shooting on Bubbling Well Road

Robbery Unsuccessful, Fled Immediately

Heavy Gunfire on Bubbling Well Road

Two Men Shot and Killed

A Female Servant Hit by Stray Bullet in the Leg

Near the Bubbling Well Road small vegetable market, at approximately 3:15 PM yesterday, police officers chased and apprehended robbers. Both sides opened fire, bullets flying across the road, killing two pedestrians. Details are as follows:

Robbers Target Clothing Store: Shao Yun Ji Clothing Store, located at No. 20 Yong An Lane, Avenue Road, is owned by Shao Yunhe from Haimen. At approximately 3:10 PM yesterday, four men suddenly entered the customer area. One stood at the doorway without entering. Of the three, one wearing a raincoat with a white silk shirt underneath, told the shopkeeper they wanted to have clothes made. The shopkeeper, noticing they were not carrying any fabric, was suspicious. As he was about to ask questions, the man pulled out a pistol and ordered them to be silent. At this time, one robber had already gone upstairs, entering the room of a Mr. Li in the pavilion. Two robbers also followed up the stairs, threatening with guns, but finding nothing of value, they went downstairs together and fled out the door.

One Robber Injured and Captured: After the robbers left the store, the clothing store staff chased after them shouting "Catch the robbers!" Police whistles and shouts followed in succession. The robbers fled north on Avenue Road, turning into Honan Road, then into Range Road. At this time, three robbers had disappeared without a trace. Only one robber was chased and captured. This robber ran to the vicinity of Hong An Lane, escaping into the Qian Yuan Rice Shop to hide temporarily. Later, he fled east onto Bubbling Well Road, firing the gun he held at the pursuing officers. The officers returned fire, hitting him in the lower abdomen. He fell to the ground and was captured.

Passersby Hit by Bullets and Killed: The location where the police fired at the robbers was near the small market. A pedestrian wearing a Zhongshan suit, who had just bought something from a pot shop, was passing by when he was hit by a stray bullet. Wounded, he fled into the Rong Xing Guan beef bun shop. Because the bullet hit his head, he died at the scene. Also, a man pushing a wheelbarrow was hit by a bullet near Hong Xing Lane, wounded in a vital area, and died immediately. Furthermore, a woman named Zhu Shen, was hit in the right leg by a stray bullet and sent to the hospital for treatment. The bodies were sent to the coroner's office to await examination today. It is said that the man in the Zhongshan suit was from Guangdong, very young. He was buying a wok lid at the pot shop, bargaining for ten cents, offering six cents, but not completing the deal. After hearing the gunshots, he suddenly crossed the road and was hit by a bullet. He was still holding several iron hooks in his hand. When he fled wounded into the Rong Xing Guan, he did not say a word, leaning against the meat-cutting board. Blood gushed from the wound in his head. In an instant, he fell to the ground and died. Zhu Shen was a nanny for the Lu family, from Ningbo, 25 years old, living in Wenyuan Lane, Xiaobeimen. At that time, she was on her way to Zhabei to take a car on her employer's order, and passed by the area when she was hit by a stray bullet. The Bubbling Well Road police chief, after the incident, immediately dispatched detectives to hunt down the fleeing robbers. It is reported that several accomplices were apprehended by evening.

Kidnappers Cruelly Throw Ransom Victim into the Huangpu River

Failed to Extort 20,000 Yuan

Eight-Year-Old Child Buried in the Belly of a Fish

Clan Leader Masterminded the Heinous Act

Zhu Songlin Provides Detailed Account of the Circumstances

Yao Jiusheng, the eight-year-old son of widow Yao Gu, residing at No. 199 Ma An Lane, Chongqing Road, was suddenly kidnapped by a gang of bandits on July 7th in front of the home of his maternal grandmother, Gu Zhao, at No. 96 Avenue Road. A letter demanding a ransom of 20,000 dollars was sent. The Jing'an Temple police station was notified. Chinese Detective Jin Yangwu and others apprehended the suspects in this case, Zhu Songlin from Pudong, and a woman, Lu Wang, etc. However, the child Yao Jiusheng has not yet been found. The details of their arrest and transfer to the First Special Court were published in this newspaper on the 11th. It is now learned that Yao Gu is only 25 years old,

Already a Widow: She has only one son. His abduction and disappearance was already extremely distressing. Fortunately, the perpetrators were arrested, making it easier to track down and rescue him, allowing them to be reunited. Who knew that terrible news would arrive? The moon would never be full again. Mother and son would never meet again. Since Yao Jiusheng was abducted, the gang of bandits, resentful over their failure to extort a ransom, actually

Threw Jiusheng into the Huangpu River: Buried in the belly of a fish. Yao Gu was overwhelmed with grief upon hearing the news, and rushed to the police station to demand a thorough investigation. Detective Jin, who was handling the case, questioned the suspect Zhu Songlin about the whereabouts of his accomplices. Zhu confessed that the mastermind behind this case was

Yao Gu's Clan Leader: A local man named Yao Zhusheng (also known as Yao Zisheng). So, at 7:45 AM the day before yesterday, Detective Jin went to No. 210 Chongqing Road and arrested Yao Zhusheng, taking him into custody at the police station. Yesterday morning, he was transferred to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special Court, where Judge Feng Shide questioned him. Wang Yaotang, the police station's lawyer, rose and stated the facts of the case, saying that the defendant Yao Zhusheng was charged with Article 373 of the Criminal Law, the crime of intimidation, Article 284, the crime of premeditated murder, and Article 2 of the Regulations for the Punishment of Kidnappers, requesting a postponement because Judge Wu Tingqi was presiding over the Zhu Songlin case, which was scheduled for a special hearing on the afternoon of the 17th, so he asked to

Postpone and Merge the Cases for Interrogation: And so on. According to Zhu Songlin's confession, he met the defendant Yao Zhusheng in Hankou Yichang. This case was also instigated by Yao. In February 29th of this year, I came to Shanghai from Pudong by boat. As soon as I landed on the Bund, I met the defendant Yao Zhusheng. After talking to each other, we agreed to meet again in the afternoon

At Yile Tian Teahouse: When I met Yao, he learned that I had not been doing well recently, so he gave me two dollars, and said he had something to discuss. He then talked about a Yao Gu in his clan, whose husband had died, fearing improper behavior, and that she was using her property to support her mother's family. He wanted me to seduce her or abduct her child, so that she would have no face to return to the Yao family, and told me that Yao Gu

Always Returned to Her Mother's Home on Saturdays: Her mother's house was located at No. 96 Avenue Road, and had extra rooms for rent. You can seize the opportunity to act. Because I was short of money, Yao gave me dozens of dollars, and I rented two rooms in the back of Gu Zhao's house, Yao Gu's mother. Later, because I saw that Yao Gu was dignified, knowledgeable, and

Did Not Behave Frivolously: I could not bear to harm her. And because the money had been spent, I moved away after living there for more than a month. Later, I met Yao Zhusheng and told him what had happened before, but Yao still ordered me to proceed. So, on July 7th, I lured her child Jiusheng out, intending to take him to Pudong temporarily. When we arrived at the Bund, we hired a sampan. Unexpectedly, at the center of the harbor, I accidentally

Lost My Grip on Jiusheng, Who Fell into the River: I was unable to save him. He drifted away without a trace. The next day, I told Yao Zhusheng about this matter. Yao gave me 25 dollars. In a few days, the money was used up again. I wrote a letter, wanting to get money from Yao Gu to make a living. Unfortunately, I was arrested. When questioned, Yao Zhusheng stated that seven years ago, when I opened a shop in Yichang, I met Yang Sen after the battle. I fled to Hankou temporarily. At that time, Zhu Songlin was

A Butcher in Hankou: And we became acquainted. Later, Zhu stole something and fled without a trace. I have never met Zhu since then. I did not instigate Zhu to abduct Yao Jiusheng. Yao Gu and I are from the same clan, and she calls me "Grandpa." Moreover, her family is not rich. How could I do such a heinous thing? I have been falsely accused. He also hired lawyer Yu Hualong to defend him. Judge Feng verified the confessions and ordered Yao to be held pending further questioning on the afternoon of the 17th, to be heard together with the Zhu Songlin case.

The Bloody Man on the Street

Seriously Injured, Silent and Uncomplaining

Mistakenly Hit with an Iron Bar

Three Suspects Arrested

On the evening of the 7th of this month, at 9:55 PM, a man from Yangzhou, Li Jinkui, was found lying on the cement sidewalk at the intersection of North Sichuan Road and Avenue Doumer, covered in blood, with a bicycle abandoned beside him. Detective No. 135 of the Avenue Doumer police station discovered him and, when questioned, he could not speak. He was taken to the police station along with his vehicle in a rickshaw. The police chief ordered him to be sent to Tongren Hospital for treatment. His head and body were seriously injured. The day before yesterday, Chinese Detective Chief Lu Gengsheng of the police station arrested the suspects Gao A'gen from Songjiang, Ren Fanrong from Shaoxing, and Cai A'lin from Tongzhou, all working as servants for Japanese at No. 175 North Sichuan Road and a Japanese-owned room. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special Court. According to the police station's lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, the victim is currently in the hospital, in serious condition. Since being admitted, he was able to say a few words on the third day, but has since been silent. Please postpone the hearing. The reason for the incident, according to the defendants, was that they had a minor dispute with a certain Ronin and were fighting. Before the matter was settled, the victim was loitering in the area on his bicycle. The defendants mistakenly believed he was an accomplice of the Ronin, so they beat him. When questioned, the three defendants Gao A'gen, etc., stated that they were employed as servants by the Japanese. Previously, they were violently beaten by thugs, so they took revenge, mistakenly injuring Li Jinkui, who was hit by an iron bar by a friend who was at large. After realizing their mistake, it was too late. They asked for leniency. Judge Shen Bingrong verified the confessions and ordered all to be remanded in custody for further questioning at a later date.

The Troubles of Taking a Concubine

Cai Shichu Attempted Suicide in the Huangpu River Because of This

The Wife Set Three Conditions

At 6:30 PM the night before last, a man over forty years old attempted suicide by jumping into the river at the Jiangxi Road Bridge, Suzhou Creek. He was rescued by a Western police officer from the water patrol, who happened to be passing by. He was taken to the police station, where he identified himself as Cai Shichu, 43 years old, from Ningbo, and owned a printing company. He lived at No. 309 and a half, Weihaiwei Road, in the Public Concession. Recently, he had taken a concubine, causing great turmoil in his family. His wife, Yang, made a lot of noise, and there was no peace. His authority as a husband declined. He felt there was no joy in the future, so he tried to kill himself by jumping into the river. The police chief sent Chinese Detective Ge Changsheng to bring his wife, Yang, to the police station. According to Yang, her husband taking a concubine was definitely with her consent beforehand, but at the time, she had set three conditions: (1) When the concubine entered the house, she should immediately give me 1,000 dollars; (2) He should not favor the concubine over his wife; (3) He should not accompany the concubine out for frivolous amusements. Her husband fully agreed to the above conditions. Unexpectedly, after time passed, her husband changed his mind. Not only had the 1,000 dollars not been received, but he accompanied the concubine to the theater and the cinema day and night, enjoying himself at will. Her hopes were completely dashed, so she cried and made a scene, not knowing that he would become so disillusioned and kill himself. The police chief, considering this a domestic dispute, advised both parties not to harm their marital relationship. He sent the original detective to escort them ashore and home.

Thugs Extorting Money

Gao Defa's Evil Nature Untamed

Wang Yanling Injured and Sues

Gao Defa (nicknamed "Big Bun"), from Jiangbei, was originally a well-known thug. After being punished by the French Concession court many times, he has now changed his profession to selling socks. However, his evil nature has not changed, and his actions are often irregular. Knowing that Wang Yanling, the owner of Wang Yan Ji Yarn Store, located in Fuxin Lane, Avenue Edward VII, was making a profit from his business, Gao went to Wang's store the day before yesterday and demanded to borrow 1,000 taels of silver. Wang refused, saying that there had never been any dealings between them. Gao left and immediately gathered more than a dozen accomplices, each carrying weapons, and waited in ambush at the entrance of Fuxin Lane. When Wang came out of the store, they dragged him away and beat him, taking Wang to the Jingchunlou Teahouse outside the Old North Gate and forcing him to sign three written agreements: (1) He was forced to sell 100 pieces of velvet yarn, paying a deposit of 350 taels of silver. If he could not sell them, he would have to compensate 50 taels of silver per piece; (2) He was forced to buy 750 pieces of waste wool. If he did not do so, he would have to compensate 3,000 taels of silver; (3) He was forced to guarantee the business of Shi Xiangchu, because Shi was currently working for Gao and had already used 200 yuan. At the time, Wang did not want to sign, but Gao slapped Wang twice. Under this oppressive force, Wang had no power to resist and had to sign. After the matter was over, he was allowed to go free. However, after being beaten by the thugs, Wang was seriously injured and immediately took a car to Dr. Qin Heqi's trauma clinic for treatment. He then hired lawyer Jin Yu and filed a complaint with the Second District Court, requesting an investigation.

Baoshan Implements Famine Relief

Advising Farmers to Plant More Wheat in Winter

Propaganda Conducted by the Agricultural Improvement Station

Using Accumulated Grain Funds to Purchase Wheat Seeds

Baoshan's agricultural products have always been 70% cotton and 30% rice. This year, due to wind and rain disasters, the cotton harvest is hopeless, and the rice harvest is poor. The livelihood of farmers is extremely difficult. It was previously decided by the county government conference to have the Agricultural Improvement Station advise farmers to plant more wheat in winter, and it was approved to allocate a portion of the accumulated grain funds to purchase wheat seeds to meet the needs of farmers. The agricultural station has already started to organize an agricultural station cooperative propaganda team with the cooperative office to go to various districts, townships, and towns to conduct practical propaganda, advise farmers to plant more wheat in winter, post slogans encouraging wheat planting, and distribute leaflets. At the same time, farmers are advised to organize production cooperatives to benefit people's livelihoods. It is reported that the agricultural station's planned propaganda work will take two weeks to complete.

The Cotton Field Disaster Situation in the Wusong District is Severe

The Wusong District Municipal Committee Office, previously reported that local wardens and farmers had sent letters reporting water shortages, with cotton fields being flooded and the autumn harvest hopeless, requesting investigation and remediation. It has been reported in this newspaper. It is now learned that the Wusong District Municipal Committee members Liu Yutong and Tang Zuanzhi, after receiving the report, immediately forwarded it to the Social Affairs Bureau, and sent staff to conduct surveys in each ward. It is estimated that in all ten wards, excluding the not yet reported Gang Zi Twenty-Five and Thirty-Two, the disaster situation in the remaining eight wards is as follows: (1) Teng Forty-One Ward, 70% or more of the households affected - 12 households, 50% or more - 7 households, less than 50% - 1 household; (2) Teng Forty Ward, 70% or more of the households affected - 122 households; (3) Teng Thirty-Nine Ward, 70% or more of the households affected - 87 households, 50% or more - 31 households, less than 50% - 1 household; (4) Gang Thirty-Three Ward, 70% or more of the households affected - 2 households, 50% or more - 34 households, less than 50% - 2 households; (5) Yi Thirty-Six Ward, 70% or more of the households affected - 4 households, 50% or more - 20 households; (6) Tui Thirty-Five Ward, 70% or more of the households affected - 86 households, 50% or more - 1 household; (7) Tui Thirty-Four Ward, 70% or more of the households affected - 67 households, 50% or more - 2 households; (8) Tui Twenty-Two Ward, 70% or more of the households affected - 55 households. The Wusong Municipal Committee Office prepared a survey register yesterday and submitted it to the Social Affairs Bureau, requesting that staff be sent to re-survey and find ways to provide relief. However, yesterday, the Wusong area was hit by strong winds and heavy rain, and the tide rose to 39 feet. The fields were flooded, and it is feared that the degree of disaster will be even greater than before. Farmers are complaining incessantly.

Cargo Transportation to Pukou Temporarily Suspended

Due to High Water and Strong Winds at the Riverside Station

The Traffic Department of the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration received a telegram from the Nanjing Riverside Station yesterday stating that due to high water and strong winds on the riverside, all cargo loaded from Shanghai should be temporarily suspended from being transported to Nanjing, and that they would be notified again to resume transportation after the water receded and the wind subsided. It is reported that the Shanghai Transportation Association and the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Transportation Association also received telegrams from the Tianjin-Pukou and Shanghai-Nanjing Transport Association, reporting the above situation. Therefore, starting yesterday, all goods loaded from Shanghai to Nanjing Riverside Station for transfer to Pukou have been temporarily suspended.

City Health Bureau Plans Vaccination

Starting October 1st

The Shanghai City Health Bureau believes that smallpox is becoming more prevalent during the winter and spring. Smallpox is a terrible disease, which can cause death or blindness. To prevent smallpox, timely vaccination is essential. The bureau's epidemic prevention section has recently planned vaccination work, stockpiling vaccine, and will start mass vaccinations from October 1st, sending doctors to schools, factories, and groups in the city to provide free vaccinations.

Bone Steaming Examination for Husband Murder Case

Yang Linxiang, a villager from Jia Yi Bridge, Caoxing District, West Shanghai, was allegedly murdered by his wife, Yang A'nan. After examination by the court, there were still doubts. The deceased's brother, Fu San, requested justice for his brother. The coffin was sealed, and a re-examination was prepared. Police Chief Liu of the Sixth District, Third Precinct of the Municipal Public Security Bureau was dispatched to arrest Yang A'nan, and together with the deceased's brother Fu San, they were sent to the court for interrogation. Prosecutor Wu has been repeatedly investigating and interrogating. According to Yang A'nan, she was not at home that day, and he actually died by hanging. She does not admit to murder. The interrogating officer verified the confession. If Yang Linxiang committed suicide by hanging, where is the rope used to cause death? Yang's wife replied that according to neighborhood customs, the rope had been burned to destroy the evidence. Also, when asked, the deceased's brother, Fu San, accused her of murder and requested redress. However, there were many doubts in this case. If Yang's wife did not intend to murder him, why did she evade the truth and flee? Furthermore, the instrument of death has been burned and destroyed, making it impossible to prove. It was heard yesterday that the court will perform a bone steaming examination to clarify the truth.

Reader Correspondence

Xia Zhonglian Asks

I am a young man of twenty. Since I was fifteen, due to livelihood issues, I left private school and went to work in business. When I was young, I was neither smart nor mischievous, but I especially liked to read novels, such as *Romance of the Three Kingdoms*, *Water Margin*, *Dream of the Red Chamber*, *Yue Fei's Biography*, etc. I have read almost all of the old novels. At the same time, I inevitably neglected my studies. Until I abandoned my studies and went into business, the knowledge I gained was nothing more than recognizing commonly used characters. When I was an apprentice, I didn't feel anything, but now, although my job is bookkeeping, my livelihood can only maintain my current state. My elderly father, weak mother, and young sister have no extra strength to care for them. Although family expenses are temporarily supported by my father's best efforts, how can I feel good about it? Solving this problem requires seeking a higher-paying career, but I am limited by my intelligence and financial resources. If I re-enter school, time and money will be difficult to come by. After much thinking, I feel that it is not too late to work hard and study hard at this time. Therefore, I would like to join a correspondence school so that I can receive appropriate guidance during my spare time (in fact, my spare time is only before 7:00 AM and after 9:00 PM). Now, what I need is knowledge of English, arithmetic, Chinese, and drawing, because I don't know any English. If I know it, I can read Western newspapers and magazines. Drawing can harmonize my temperament and can also be used to help me make a living. Arithmetic seems to be a required item for entering any school. Chinese naturally needs to be studied in depth. Which of these four correspondence schools is the most complete? Are there any books on this subject that are easy to use for self-study? Please advise.

(Reply) It is very good that you are determined to study in your spare time. This is the only way for you. I hope you first make a decision.

English must be at a considerable level before you can do correspondence study. If you don't know anything, it's very difficult. We think it's not the most important thing for your needs. Chinese and arithmetic are very important. You should focus on the applied aspects. The Commercial Press Correspondence School on Baoshan Road, Shanghai has these two subjects. You can request a copy of the regulations. If you are satisfied, you can try it. If you have never studied painting, it may not be easy to do correspondence study either. I just don't know how your talent is for this subject.

Yu Kongzhang Asks

I was forced to study business in the grocery industry due to my childhood environment. Now I work in this industry, filling the position of bookkeeping clerk. I feel that I lack both the knowledge and experience of the commercial future. I have repeatedly wanted to study, but I lack a suitable direction and opportunity. Since I have already studied business, I must pursue in-depth study in business. Observing the current era of commercial competition, if businessmen have simple minds, no vision, and no fresh ideas, they will surely fail. Therefore, the knowledge and experience of businessmen are very important, and there is a real need to engage in research. I am now planning to use my spare time to supplement my studies with a kind of practical knowledge related to business and more progressive. However, limited by the economic strength of our shop assistants, it is questionable how to obtain this kind of practical knowledge that is pertinent to business. I sincerely request that you give me appropriate direction, or what subjects to study on my own to make up for my shortcomings, and I hope you will reply in the newspaper.

(Reply) According to your current environment, it is best to supplement your studies in your spare time. You can refer to the reply to Xia Jun's question above. The Commercial Press Correspondence School also has a business department, but the lowest business preparatory course requires at least four or five years of English level, which may not be very suitable for you. We think Chinese and arithmetic are still important, but you should focus on application. There is also one more thing, since you are a bookkeeper, bookkeeping correspondence is also suitable. The Lixin Accountant Firm at No. 452 Jiangxi Road, Shanghai, was founded by accountant Pan Xulun, and has an affiliated accounting correspondence school. You can request a copy of the regulations. If you are satisfied, you can try it.

Correspondence Stamp

Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau Relieves West District Dairy Farms of Cattle Plague

Some dairy farms in this city suffered from cattle plague last month, especially the cattle at Chen Mujin's Dairy Shed on Route Cardinal Mercier, with the most severe illness. Of the ten dairy cows, all were seriously ill. Before the owner of the dairy shed went to the Commodity Inspection Bureau to request veterinarians to diagnose and treat them, two dairy cows worth 500 yuan died. There were still five cows suffering from diarrhea and loss of appetite, with very high body temperatures, and milk production completely stopped. After injecting serum, the diarrhea stopped in six days, appetite increased, and milk production returned to normal. They have now fully recovered. The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau is very willing to provide this kind of service and hopes that all milk companies will contact the bureau at any time to arrange for preventive cattle plague injections to avoid spreading the disease.

Verdict to be Announced in Case of Police Officer Shooting and Killing Shop Employee

Le Ke Rang, a patrolman from the Second Precinct of the First District in the city, was playing with Ding Lianchang, an employee of the Old Parade Ground Shoe Store, when a bullet was accidentally fired, killing Ding. The Public Security Bureau sent Le to the local court, where the prosecutor investigated and filed charges. Yesterday, Judge Zhao Yongzhou opened the court. According to Le's testimony, at 9:40 PM on August 8th, I saw more than 20 people gathered together in the Old Parade Ground, and suspected they were bandits, so I went with live ammunition to disperse them. Later, when I was removing the bullet, it accidentally fired, mistakenly injuring Ding Lianchang. The judge said that Huang Lianfu, the owner of the shoe store, had long stated in the investigation court that you aimed the gun and played with it, causing it to fire, and you loaded the bullet yourself, so how could you not know about unloading it? He then summoned the deceased's younger brother, Ding Miaosheng, to testify. I did not witness my brother's death. The shop owner Huang Lianfu testified that he was not in the store at the time, and that the police officer did not intend to do it. So-called he was unlucky, and the deceased was also unlucky. The judge asked if he had already received compensation for the private settlement for the previous statement of accidentally shooting and killing? (Answer) Yes. Then, he asked prosecutor Yang Qi for his opinion, who said that the defendant aimed and shot, hence the injury to the head, and his gun was very good, so it would not misfire. Please make a judgment according to the law. The interrogating officer announced the end of the debate and scheduled the verdict to be announced tomorrow. The defendant was remanded in custody.

Owen Dies

Owen, a mechanical engineer at the Dredging Bureau, was shot several times when he was distributing wages on a dredger. He recovered at a public hospital and returned to his country for recuperation. Leaking the Secret Method of Manufacturing Rubber Shoes

Da Zhonghua Factory Accuses Xue Fuxiang

Jiangnan Factory Suspected of Collusion

Xue Fuxiang, a technician at the Da Zhonghua Rubber Factory on Xujiahui Road in the French Concession, recently secretly informed the Jiangnan Rubber Factory of the factory's secret method for manufacturing galoshes and entered into a contract. This was discovered by Wu Zhesheng, the manager of Da Zhonghua, who retained lawyer Lin Yingqing to file a lawsuit with the French Concession police. After the captain dispatched detectives to arrest Xue, he was escorted to the Second Special District Court yesterday, where Judge Luo Renji of the Criminal Division interrogated him. First, Fei Xizhen, the police lawyer, explained the case, stating that the prosecution was based on Articles 335 and 366 of the Criminal Law, "Obstructing Secrets" and "Breach of Trust," requesting an investigation. In addition, the plaintiff Wu Zhesheng's lawyer stated that the defendant was an assistant technician at the Da Zhonghua Rubber Factory and was instigated by the owner of the Jiangnan Rubber Factory on Wuhua Road to leak the secret manufacturing method of Da Zhonghua's galoshes. A witness, Xu Zengyuan, saw the defendant boiling oil and mixing ingredients at the Jiangnan Factory on the 13th. It was found that the Jiangnan Factory actually colluded with the defendant to enter into a contract. The wording of the first two articles clearly instigates the theft of Da Zhonghua's trade secrets. This manufacturing method is a technology that Da Zhonghua obtained after expending great effort and spending 50,000 yuan of national currency. Once leaked, not only will the factory's capital be shaken, but more than 2,000 workers will also be affected. He requested a strict investigation according to law, etc. After Judge Luo asked the defendant's age and address, he ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody and await a later hearing.

Zhang Weihan's Remarks After Returning to Shanghai

Did Not Take Up Position as Counselor in the Civil Affairs Bureau

Will Move to Suzhou to Study

Mr. Zhang Weihan, the commissioner of the Yunnan Province and director of the Department of Civil Affairs, returned to Shanghai from Beijing yesterday. A reporter from the New Shanghai News, having read reports that he had experienced a scare in Beijing, went to his residence to interview him. Mr. Zhang received him and was editing his old poetry manuscripts, appearing very leisurely. After exchanging pleasantries, they began to talk. Reporter (Q): The newspaper reported that you had a scare in Beijing. What was the misunderstanding? Zhang (A): This matter was due to the Beijing Garrison Headquarters receiving a telegram from the Hankou Garrison Headquarters stating that a certain Zhang from Hubei Province, who had committed a crime, had fled to Beijing and was staying at Room 33 of the Central Hotel. They requested a swift investigation and arrest. Because my surname was the same, my accent was close to that of Hubei, and I happened to be staying in Room 336, I was mistaken by the intelligence officers of the headquarters. They came to interrogate me without first investigating the details. Their handling of the matter was too careless. Commander Sheng Gu Zheng Lun has already dismissed and punished those involved. I have not taken it to heart. (Q): What was your mission in Beijing this time? Did you meet with Chairman Chiang? (A): I was only there to attend the state funeral of the late President Tan. I had no other mission, so I did not visit the Chairman. I only visited Tan's tomb. (Q): The newspaper reported that the National Government appointed you as a counselor in the Civil Affairs Bureau. Have you taken office? (A): The National Government originally planned to appoint one counselor from each province to the Civil Affairs Bureau to provide advice on local conditions. When I participated in the drafting of the treaty with Vietnam in Beijing the year before last, I had already recommended a suitable person to fill the position. This person is sufficient to provide advice. Zhang also said that he had been in politics for many years and felt quite tired. His current situation is difficult, but his desire to study has not diminished. Yesterday, he passed through Suzhou and a friend helped him rent several rooms in a garden. He considered it very suitable for reading and will move there to study and rest.

General Manager Guo of China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Responds to Seven Demands of Dockworkers

Bonuses and Meals Cannot Be Handled at Present

Dismissal and Employment Are Administrative Prerogatives

Since the dockworkers of the five wharves of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company raised seven demands, including giving bonuses, providing meals, reinstating old workers, and dismissing new workers, the Social Bureau has ordered both parties to negotiate on their own. Yesterday, General Manager Guo of the company responded to the seven demands item by item. The following is a special excerpt. We have received your letter and listed seven demands, which have all been read. The replies are as follows: (1) Regarding the request to grant bonuses according to the principle of equality, the case of the bonus dispute issued by former Commissioner Li is still under consideration by this office. We will report it to the National Government in the future, and we should wait patiently for the National Government's instructions. This case has not been resolved at all, and it is impossible to handle it at present. (2) Regarding the issue of providing meals, firstly, there has been no precedent for providing meals for decades. Secondly, there are too many warehouse workers. At a time when the company's finances are stretched, it is really impossible to suddenly increase the huge burden. We can only discuss it at length after future economic conditions improve. (3) The transfer of Wu Bingru and others to other positions is either for promotion or for mutual transfer to warehouses to increase experience, which is absolutely beneficial to the individuals being promoted. Why is it considered inappropriate? According to the positions of the warehouse staff, promotion to the five warehouses has always been the practice, especially the South Warehouse. This is purely an administrative prerogative of the company in employing people. Now, your association is interfering, which is beyond the scope of protecting workers. Even in the previously agreed treatment conditions, there is no provision that promotions cannot be made. This request is unreasonable. (4) The dismissal of Zhou Xinbao and the other four people was confirmed to be due to theft of goods and cannot be compared to unwarranted dismissal. It is a matter of course that warehouse staff should conduct themselves with integrity, cherish their reputation, and jointly promote the business of the warehouse. There is no room for pretense. Now, your association does not punish the warehouse staff who stole the goods, which is already strange. Instead, you are protecting them, which is tantamount to deliberately destroying the reputation of the company's warehouse business. The company really cannot bear the sorrow. (5) If there are shortages of goods in each warehouse, the company should appoint new people to fill the vacancies. This is the company's administrative power to employ people. It is clearly stipulated in Article 1 of the previously agreed regulations. Moreover, the appointed staff are all assistants and have considerable ability. They can be competent under the guidance of the supervisors. The so-called "unfamiliar with the wharf situation" is too empty and cannot be a reason. It is close to intentional exclusion. (6) The company can order the warehouse managers to notify the workers who have not joined the association. However, if they voluntarily do not join the association, it is a matter for the individual to handle. The company cannot force them. If they have not committed any faults, how can they be dismissed because of this? Moreover, if they do not join the association, they will not be able to enjoy the protection of your association in the future. It is their own abandonment of benefits and does not harm your association in any way. (7) This article can instruct the warehouse managers to investigate the residential status of the dependents and order them to move. If they do not comply, consider punishment. Immediate dismissal is too harsh and unfair. In short, the commissioner has always had the intention of protecting the workers. All the bad treatments or reasonable requests will be happily adopted. However, if they exceed the proper limits and are close to threats, it will be difficult to accept. According to the company's environment in recent years, we have been struggling in difficult circumstances every day. At this time, the personnel of the whole company, both inside and outside, should work together to endure and maintain each other, so that we can gradually progress to a bright future and achieve a prosperous period. If we only indulge in emotional impulses and strive for contention, I am afraid that the overall situation is in danger. If the skin does not exist, what will the fur attach to? If that time comes, your association members will be too late to regret it. We all belong to the same family. I sincerely express my heartfelt words. I hope you will consider it together. This is addressed to the Workers' Association of the Five Wharves.

Coal Industry: The Shanghai Coal Industry Trade Association telegraphed: To all compatriots of agriculture, industry, commerce, study, and soldiers: Tracing back to the Manchus entering the customs and seizing sovereignty, the hatred of the Ming Dynasty originated from internal strife. The Qing Emperor was licentious and extravagant in governing, dividing the territory, and losing national sovereignty. In the past three hundred years, mud and sand have been exhausted. Our General Sun was deeply afraid of the nation's demise, advocated a national revolution, struggled for more than twenty years, traveled millions of miles, embraced love, and worked hard until the Xinhai Revolution, creating the Republic of China. It went through Yuan's claim to the throne and warlords fighting. It marked the establishment of the system to destroy the rebellion and accommodate the Communist Party to appease the people. The vision is far-reaching and will last forever. Now, the heavens are unkind, and the General has passed away. For six years since then, the smoke of war has not ceased. The scourge of drought has not subsided, and the disaster of floods has spread. The Central Plains has been submerged, and the number of starving people in the disaster area has reached 60 million for two months. Speaking of drought, the afforestation policy is lost. Speaking of flooding, the water control policy is dead. The act of dismantling has not been promoted, and the implementation of the Three People's Principles is pending. Suddenly, there is news of war in Guangdong and Guangxi, and war in Xiang and Gan. The sound is broadcast, and the heartstrings are about to break. Alas, who has no brothers, such as feet and hands, and who has no husband and wife, such as guests and friends. May I ask in the rain of bullets, who is willing to be forgiving? Thinking of boiling beans to burn stalks, I am ridiculed by barbarians. How can I bear to let the people of water and fire be in an eternal abyss? Do not teach the red and white foreign invaders to penetrate into the heart. Shanghai coal merchants, seeing this crisis, cannot help but be horrified. Thinking of turning war into peace, I used telegrams to express my feelings, praying to embrace love, implement the Three People's Principles, work together in harmony, quickly achieve equality and freedom, clumsy writing is difficult to stretch, and the main points are not complicated. I deeply hope that we will all share peace and harmony, and we will get the national welfare. Lin Dian is frightened, and I pray for public consideration. Shanghai Coal Industry Trade Association, delete.

Tea Industry: The Nanshi Tea Industry Association held its 22nd executive committee meeting yesterday. (1) Because the spring tea production this year was poor and the source price was high, the price was revised. The minimum price of 30 cents per catty was removed, that is, the original price of 35 cents per catty was the minimum. Some colleagues still sell 3 catties for one yuan according to their usual habits. Other colleagues and shops believe that this violates the regulations and disputes arise. Yesterday, the association, in order to be cautious, requested the city chamber of commerce to send personnel to the meeting for guidance in advance. Yesterday, Xue Guangqian, a representative of the city chamber of commerce, attended the meeting and had a long discussion. It was decided that the association would issue a notice, clarifying the facts, and the minimum price is 35 cents per catty, and each yuan still sells 3 catties. If any store objects to 3 catties per yuan, they must send a letter to the meeting with the reasons for the objection. If there is no reply after receiving the notice, it will be deemed as tacit consent. (2) Recently, the flood area in various provinces has been large, and various public offices are conducting fundraising for disaster relief. Colleagues in our industry also have this intention. However, how should the solicitation process be carried out? It was decided to publicly recommend Yang Shangting, Hu Jianchen, and other eight people from the executive committee to solicit donations separately, only soliciting donations from colleagues in the industry. Once the collection is completed, it will be distributed to various disaster relief agencies. The meeting adjourned at 6:00 p.m.

Free Talk

Random Musings from the B陰庭艸齋 Studio

Old Wu's Vernacular Literature

One day, I encountered Old Wu in an alleyway selling baked sweet potatoes. He had six bamboo skewers representing six prize levels: horse, cow, sheep, chicken, dog, and pig. I saw that the "pig" was the character 字, and I suspected he had been influenced by the New Literature. But then I saw the character "dog" and suspected he still had affection for the Old Literature. Out of curiosity, I asked him why he changed "豕" (shǐ, ancient word for pig) but not "犬" (quǎn, dog). Only then did I realize he was a representative of an incomplete literary reformer. This is a playful poem I sent to Old Wu:

"Old Wu sells sweet potatoes,

Drawing lots determines the winner.

Lots are divided into 'horse', 'cow', 'sheep',

And also 'chicken', 'dog', 'pig'.

I advise changing 'dog' to 'hound',

He says he must follow the book.

I say, the book uses '豕',

Not your 'pig'.

Like a woman with bound feet,

Wanting to become a woman with unbound feet.

Counting the peaches and plums,

Old Wu surpasses Old Hu."

The "Dwarf" Tomb of Nantong

— Yin Shouman

During the late Ming Dynasty, the Central Plains were rife with troubles. Japanese pirates seized the opportunity to invade, and the coastal areas of Jiangsu and Zhejiang were repeatedly ravaged. They plundered, raped, and did everything imaginable. The people suffered greatly from their calamities. One day, more than five hundred Japanese pirates invaded the southern suburbs of Nantong. The government troops, fearing their power, dared not resist and simply closed the city to await reinforcements. At that time, there was a flour merchant named Cao Ding, skilled in martial arts and extraordinarily brave. Witnessing this situation, he was greatly angered and exclaimed, "Are we, the subjects of the majestic Ming Dynasty, willing to accept such humiliation? How can we face our ancestors in the afterlife?" He then gathered over a hundred strong men from the village, organized them into a unit, and explained the righteousness of the cause. All were moved and swore to live or die together. Cao then tied flour knives to the ends of sticks to use as weapons and used horses that ground flour as mounts. After the preparations were complete, he mounted a horse, brandished his knife, and led the team straight into the enemy's camp. Caught off guard, the enemy suspected that a flying general had descended from the sky and fell into confusion and disarray. The government troops inside the city responded, and the momentum increased. Most of the enemy was annihilated, and the rest fled in panic. Cao pursued them for thirty li (a unit of distance) (a place name). Suddenly, it rained heavily, and the horse became trapped in a muddy pit and could not get out, and Cao was killed. The villagers were grateful for his righteousness and bravery and built a shrine and erected a statue at the foot of Wolf Mountain to commemorate him. They also buried the Japanese corpses north of the shrine, which is now the "Dwarf" Tomb. It is estimated to be four zhang (a unit of height) high and about four mu (a unit of area) wide. The late sage Zhang Jian specially built a pavilion on top of it as a place for tourists to rest, naming it Jingguan. This was intended to signify the accumulation of corpses and sealed earth to represent the achievements of the battle. In the eleventh year of the Republic of China, more than ten Japanese naval officers came to Tong to sightsee. Seeing this historical site, they thought it harmed the national image and wanted to move the remains back to their country. After being politely refused by local people, they left reluctantly.

Jiang Kanghu Doesn't Forget His Motherland

— Xu Wancheng

On the 12th of this month at noon, I accompanied Mr. Huang Jingwan to visit Dr. Jiang Kanghu, who had recently returned from the United States. We talked for quite a while. Mr. Jiang has been away from the country for five years. This time, he will only stay for less than a month before going west again. This trip is purely for sightseeing in his motherland and catching up with friends and relatives.

Mr. Jiang is a honorary consultant at the Library of Congress in Washington D.C., a special lecturer at the University of Oregon, and the director of a professor at McGill University in Canada. He signed a "lifelong" contract. Mr. Jiang is the only Chinese person to serve as the director of a professor at a university in the United States. Mr. Jiang recently wrote "An Outline of Chinese Culture" in English and translated "Three Hundred Tang Poems," which was published in New York in the United States.

Mr. Jiang said, "I (Jiang refers to himself this way below) live a comfortable life in the United States and am content to stay. However, I hear about the natural disasters and man-made calamities befalling my motherland, and I feel saddened. I am also a member of the Chinese nation. Living a carefree life overseas, I cannot bear to see my compatriots suffering. I plan to return to China in a few years, dedicate myself to academics, live a simple life, and share the hardships with my compatriots." From this, we can see that Mr. Jiang has not forgotten his motherland.

Mr. Jiang had previously met with the deposed Emperor Xuantong. This time, upon returning to China, he was also summoned by Chairman Chiang. On the evening of the 13th, he went to Nanjing with Mr. Chu Minyi, a member of the Central Committee, and spoke with Chairman Chiang. He said that he has "pure intentions and does not harbor any ulterior motives."

New Anecdotes of Ronghu

— Jing Mengdie

The Vicissitudes of the Streets: The terrain of Wuxi city is relatively low. Therefore, when floods come, the streets inside and outside the city along the river are completely submerged in water, forming a vast expanse with no boundaries. There is a sense of vicissitudes in the city. In order to maintain transportation, the citizens set up long wooden planks everywhere, like the double rails of a railway. Peddlers travel back and forth on them, looking like a dragon palace in the sea. Although the water has receded in some areas, it is still difficult to walk because the streets of Wuxi, except for a few roads, are mostly paved with bricks. After being submerged in water for many days, they have undergone changes, either protruding or sinking. The ground level has long been destroyed, like the rugged mountain roads of Sichuan, making people sigh that it is impossible to walk. Some citizens have written to the authorities, requesting that repairs be carried out quickly, as this is an important municipal matter. Otherwise, the transformation of hills and valleys is only a matter of time.

The World of Tanchun Opera: Apart from the scenery of the lakes and mountains, Wuxi lacks entertainment venues. Although there have been a few theaters, they have been intermittent and are now extinct. When Beijing opera transformed into movies, the Zhongnan and Wuxi theaters emerged in response, and the people's attention was focused on the silver screen. Recently, there has been another transformation into Tanchun opera. The Zhongdong Theater took the lead, and it was packed every night. Soon, everyone saw it as a speculative business. As a result, the First Theater, the Xinmin Theater, and the Dahua Theater sprang up one after another, all making profits three times over. The plays performed include "The Pearl Pagoda," "Double Pearl Phoenix," "The Jade Dragonfly," "Liang Shanbo," and "Diao Nanlou." Posters are visible everywhere in the streets. The troupe is not called Tanchun opera but Southern Opera. All the gongs, drums, costumes, and scenery are the same as in traditional operas, but the singing and dialogue are still in Tanchun. This is truly a new face for this genre. The lyrics are crude and vulgar, but the emotions are poignant and touching, fully deserving of the words "sad, sentimental, stubborn, and beautiful." It is especially welcomed by women. It is emotionally moving and unforgettable, and even rain cannot stop it. Therefore, there is a woman in the west gate, a young unmarried woman, who, in her beautiful youth, was moved by the enchanting melodies of the Huangpu River and became so infatuated that she went mad. The newspapers reported it, and the neighbors laughed. This shows the magic of Tanchun opera.

World Small Events Record

Female Police in London: In several major cities in Europe and America, great importance is attached to police administration, and all facilities are extremely complete. In addition to male police officers, there are also female police officers, but the number is still not large. Taking London, the capital of England, as an example, female police officers began to be hired before 1925, totaling 24. They were assigned to various services and achieved good results. Soon, the number was increased to 50, and now there are 100.

Private Animal Garden: In a dairy farm in London, there is a horse breeder who is gentle and likes to be with birds and animals. In addition to 100 horses that he raises and watches over, there are two Indian monkeys and a tamed wild rabbit. He often takes a female fox with him to stroll around London, just like people take their pet dogs for a walk. In addition, there are many rabbits, pigeons, canaries, and exotic birds from foreign countries. The sound of birds singing and animals calling all day long is very lively. This place is like a private animal garden. (Haiker)

A Record of Diving Skills

— Mo Yi

The world champion diver, the Frenchman Maitrejean, has arrived in Shanghai and will perform his amazing skills at the Carnival. At that time, the people of Shanghai will have another feast for the eyes. The Continental Daily has published a brief history of Maitrejean and his skills. The following is a translated excerpt:

Maitrejean's father was originally an athlete, especially skilled in swimming. Therefore, Maitrejean was often taken to the swimming pool by his father when he was two years old. He became interested in swimming through constant exposure and has achieved today's honor. His first diving test was from a height of about seven to nine feet. Although the height increased day by day, there were many times when it was doubled. His heart was always excited by this, so he worked harder. Today, he can dive from a height of 105 feet into water that is only five feet deep and hold the world championship. His fame began when he defeated a famous diver in a public performance in Mexico. Afterwards, he defeated several divers, and his reputation grew. At the same time, due to difficult living conditions, he became a professional diver. According to him, "I have been a professional diver for thirty-four years. In the past ten years, I have often thought about stopping this profession, but my wife does not think so. She says that my energy has not declined and that there is still the possibility of continuing for another ten years. If that is the case, then I will be sixty-seven years old. I cannot help but laugh when I think of an old man with white hair competing with young children." Diving can sometimes be very dangerous. Therefore, when Maitrejean dived into the water from a bridge 136 feet high, he injured his left arm. At that time, he was young and did not care. He continued to do it the next day. As a result, the arm injury became more serious, and he also injured his forehead. He was hospitalized for more than a month before he recovered. Other accidents are too numerous to count.

Maitrejean has an amazing skill: diving from the end of a 105-foot ladder in the style of a seabird. As soon as his feet leave the ladder, he is as fast as a falcon. When he reaches the middle, he does a somersault and then dives into the water in a dangerous manner. This skill has been performed many times in Spain, England, the United States, and France and has won much praise. The martial arts movie star Douglas Fairbanks especially praised it. Another of Maitrejean's skills is slow-motion diving. He is as light as a leaf, drifting down, looking like a kite. The posture is extremely beautiful, but it is more difficult than fast-motion diving because it is difficult to maintain the balance and center of gravity of the body while drifting down slowly, and there is a risk of colliding with the edge of the pool or the bottom. Maitrejean said, "When diving into the water from a very high altitude, the eardrums are often struck by the air during the descent, so I have severe hearing loss and there is no way to treat it."

Records of Sights and Sounds in the Old Capital

— Zhu An

Sandflies

The south is full of poisonous insects, plants, and trees. Therefore, Changli (Han Yu) has the line "fearing medicine when getting out of bed." The northern capital has a cold climate, so there should be no such problem. However, in the middle of summer, there are also one or two things to worry about, namely geckos and scorpions, which are especially poisonous. Their shape is like pincers with hooked tails, and the tails contain poisonous juice. They sting people with their tails, causing unbearable pain. The ancient character 萬 (wàn, ten thousand) is a representation of their shape. Later, the radical 虫 (chóng, insect) was added to create the character 蠆 (chài, scorpion). It is actually the same thing. One summer, I was temporarily living in Professor Wang's residence at Yenching University. During a daytime nap, I heard rustling sounds by my pillow, but I didn't think much of it. At night, when I unfolded my quilt, there was a scorpion there! I was so terrified that I could hardly sleep. This room had screens and was cleaned thoroughly, but it was still unavoidable. The situation in other places can be imagined. Therefore, those who live in the north should either use a mosquito net or move their beds to the center of the room, away from the walls. However, these creatures cannot kill people with their sting. Modern biologists have long determined this, so there is nothing to worry about. The only thing that humans cannot control is the sandfly. Sandflies are slender and white. They fly and gather on people's skin, almost invisible to the eye. Newcomers are bitten the most severely. In the second year, resistance gradually increases, and those who have lived there for a long time gradually become unafraid. However, those whose blood is easily reactive may never be spared. Xiehe Hospital (Peking Union Medical College Hospital) has studied this phenomenon extensively but has not found a cure. Recently, it has been discovered that the source of sandflies is the Reclining Buddha Temple in the Western Hills. It is said that covering the streams with lime during the spring season may eradicate their roots. In the future, with municipal improvements and the elimination of filth, human effort may not be able to overcome nature.

Daifu (Doctor)

In the northern dialect, doctors are called Daifu (大夫). However, the 大 (dà, big) is pronounced as dài. Southerners often find this strange. However, this pronunciation is very accurate. Da is in the Tai rhyme (泰韻), and the ancient pronunciation should be dài. The current common pronunciation of dà, with a departing tone like the character 達 (dá), is influenced by the Wu dialect. In the Wu dialect, all characters in the Tai rhyme are pronounced in the Ma rhyme (禡韻). It is unknown why, but northerners specifically adopted this Wu dialect pronunciation, while still pronouncing the proper noun Daifu as the correct pronunciation. The same is true for place names. Datong (大同) and Daming (大名) are both pronounced Dàitong (代同) and Dàiming (代名). Ignorant people do not know this and consider the Ma rhyme to be correct and the Tai rhyme to be erroneous, so they shake their heads in confusion. Calling doctors Daifu may also be considered strange. However, it is not known that ancient official titles, used respectfully for a long time, have become customary forms of respect. The title for barbers is Daizhao (待詔), the title for tea servers is Boshi (博士), and the title for pawnbrokers is Chaofeng (朝奉). To extend this, Xianggong (相公) was a title used by the Tang people to respect the prime minister, but after the Ming Dynasty, it was used to call scholars. This is a pre-blessing. Yuanyuan (員外) was a scattered official title in the Tang and Song dynasties, almost available to everyone. Wealthy people in the countryside then usurped this honorific title. Therefore, in novels, local tyrants are always called Yuanyuan. This is an abuse. As for calling doctors Daifu, there is also an explanation. In ancient times, those who practiced medicine had to be connected to the government. The Golden Lotus and Dream of the Red Chamber mention seeking medical treatment and always say to invite a certain Taiyi (太醫, imperial physician). In the beginning, all doctors were Daifu. Subsequently, everyone called doctors Daifu, just like southerners call doctors Langzhong (郎中).

Rotary Club Novel

A Husband's Wife (14)

— Jiang Hongjiao

His goals and hopes increased and progressed step by step. Initially, he was naturally limited to spiritual comfort, which was already very satisfying. Because the other party's defenses were lax, his imagination gradually turned to physical desires. Mrs. Chen originally did not have a firm will. When she was in love with Mr. Li, she only pursued the individual pleasures of a boastful and seemingly comfortable life. She only felt that Mr. Chen was a restrained moralist who did not know how to enjoy life or make money, especially not enough money to provide for her use. Therefore, she was not satisfied with such a young husband. Her association with Mr. Li was just a kind of social interaction, and she thought it was ordinary social interaction. Because she did not have many friends, she wanted to use Mr. Li to get to know more friends. She herself was not prepared to fall in love with Mr. Li and did not expect to be conquered by Mr. Li's inch-by-inch strategy.

One day, it was Sunday, and Mr. Chen, as usual, did not leave the house. He thought that his wife must be very busy and going out to play with her friends. The night before, he had asked Mrs. Li to buy a lot of food, so he could comfortably eat a meal at home. Who knew that his wife would not go out and would sleep until noon without getting up. Usually, Mrs. Li would clean the house after Mrs. Chen went out, but today, Mrs. Li did not come in to avoid suspicion. The floor was covered with melon seed shells and candy wrappers. Mrs. Chen reached out from the quilt and grabbed a cigarette from the cigarette jar, lit it, and smoked it to her heart's content. Mr. Chen was really restless. He did not dare to urge his wife to get up, but just paced around the room. Who knew that his foot would step on the residue of bubble gum and stick to it.

"Damn it!" he muttered angrily.

"Who brought you bad luck?" Mrs. Chen said from the bed with her eyes closed.

"You can get up now. The Li family has already had lunch. After you get up, you can clean the house. There's bubble gum all over my feet."

"Do you know what time I came back and what time I fell asleep?"

"Then you're awake now."

"Can't I rest for a while?" She threw the cigarette butt on the ground and went back to sleep under the covers. Mr. Chen sighed and saw that there was still more than half of the cigarette left on the ground, so he picked it up, put it out, and placed it on the ashtray.

Relief: Starting yesterday, we have begun collecting items. All sectors and members who wish to donate, regardless of gender, age, or size, old clothes, shoes, hats, etc., can be sent directly to the association.

Joint Fundraising Meeting of Shanghai Guilds and Public Associations: The Shanghai Guilds and Public Associations held a temporary member meeting the day before yesterday to discuss the donation methods of various organizations. Attendees included Wang Xiaoyu, Chen Liangyu, Guo Zhongliang, Wu Shutian, and dozens of others. Chen Liangyu chaired the meeting. After the formal opening ceremony, the discussion was immediately launched. Wang Xiaoyu proposed that guilds and public associations with rental income should allocate one or two months' rent to the relief efforts. Those with no rental income or very little should donate appropriately. Chen Liangyu proposed that organizations that have already voluntarily donated funds to relief agencies should consider making additional donations under the name of the joint association and report the amount of previous voluntary donations to the association for verification. Wu Shutian proposed that representatives of various organizations should go back to hold meetings and submit their decisions, the amount they have committed to donate, and the funds to the joint association within a week, so that the total amount can be compiled and forwarded to the various provincial flood relief committees. The chairman summarized the proposals and put them to a vote, which was unanimously passed. The joint association will notify all affiliated organizations to act accordingly.
