Siam Restricts Overseas Chinese

Amended Immigration Regulations Increase Entry Fees

Chinese Chamber of Commerce's Efforts to Argue Against Were Ineffective, Now Implemented

National Federation of Chambers of Commerce Cables Requesting Negotiations

The Siamese General Chamber of Commerce of China sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday, saying, "Dear Sirs, The Siamese government's Ministry of Interior promulgated the Amended Immigration Regulations of Buddhist Era 2474 and the Enforcement Law of the Immigration Regulations on August 15th, stipulating an increase in the entry fees for foreigners, to be implemented three months after the date of promulgation. Foreigners returning to their home countries must obtain a return-to-Siam passport from the Siamese government upon leaving Siam and pay a handling fee. This took effect on August 17th, etc. The association found that these newly promulgated regulations are related to our overseas Chinese. We tried in various ways beforehand to cancel the regulations or reduce the fees, but our power was limited and we were ultimately unsuccessful. Now that the regulations and enforcement law have been formally promulgated, in addition to translating them and sending them to the municipal chambers of commerce in coastal cities for the information of overseas Chinese merchants, we enclose the translated texts of the immigration regulations and enforcement law for your perusal and dissemination to all overseas Chinese merchants. Yours, etc." The regulations are appended below:

Immigration Regulations (1) These regulations are named the Amended Immigration Regulations of 2474. (2) These regulations will take effect three months after the date of promulgation in the Official Gazette. (3) For Article 6 of the Immigration Regulations of 2470, the following amendments are made: Those who have one of the following circumstances regarding entry are not allowed to enter: (1) Those who do not have a formal passport from their government or a formal passport recognized by the Siamese government. (2) Those who are sick. (3) Those who have not been vaccinated or are unwilling to be vaccinated. (4) Those who have no occupation and no one to support them, or those who are found by a doctor to be physically or mentally unsound. (5) Those of bad character, who are believed to cause public unrest after arriving in Siam. (6) Those who are unable to pay the immigration entry tax. Regarding Article 1, if there is no passport, the Siamese government may issue an entry passport. In addition to ambassadors or representatives of various countries coming to Siam, or crew members of ships or airplanes in transit, who are exempt from passports, there are also the following two types who are exempt from passports: (A) Those passing through on long-distance trains. (B) Those temporarily traveling back and forth across the Siamese border. (4) After entering Siam, the place of residence must be reported to the government, which will issue a license. Men and women under the age of twelve are not subject to this rule. From the date of the announcement of these regulations, foreigners who wish to return to their home countries must report to the government and obtain a license in Siam. In the future, after returning to Siam, they must submit the return-to-Siam license to the county government for review and approval. Even if they have a return-to-Siam license, if the government deems them to be undesirable elements, the Siamese government may cancel their license and not allow them to come to Siam. (5) The following people coming to Siam are not subject to these regulations: (A) Ambassadors or representatives of various countries coming to Siam. (B) Foreigners temporarily coming to Siam who are not staying for a long time or doing business or opening factories, etc. (6) Those who violate these regulations and enter are considered guilty. The Siamese government may impose a fine of up to 1,000 yuan. (7) The Minister of Interior is in charge of implementing the enforcement measures for these regulations.

Detailed Rules of Enforcement: On the date of the promulgation of the Amended Immigration Regulations of 2474, the Siamese Ministry of Interior simultaneously announced a departmental order, stipulating the detailed rules of enforcement for the immigration regulations. The following is a translation of the detailed rules of enforcement: The Ministry of Interior, in accordance with the provisions of Article 18 of the Third Amended Immigration Export Regulations, promulgates the detailed rules of enforcement of the Immigration Regulations as follows: (1) Foreigners entering the country who are deemed inadmissible may be temporarily detained in a specific place and immediately deported. (2) If there are too many people without passports, and officials cannot investigate them all at once, they may be temporarily detained at a designated location or issued a temporary license. Even if foreigners coming to Siam have foreign passports that are not issued by the Siamese government, the Siamese government may temporarily allow them to enter, but they must report their place of residence to the Siamese government within 48 hours. (3) Those with temporary licenses or return-to-Siam licenses may be required by the government to formally register with the county government within a specified time. (4) All entrants must submit two photographs, seven centimeters long and six centimeters wide, to the government. (5) Fees: (A) Pay a photo and handling fee of ten baht and submit it to the government to issue an entry passport. This passport is valid for two years. (B) This passport can still be used when foreigners return to their home countries, but they must obtain a return-to-Siam passport from the Siamese government when leaving Siam and pay a handling fee of five baht. (C) After entering the country, they must report their place of residence to the government, which will issue a residence permit, with a fee of 30 baht. (6) Cancel Article 17 of the immigration regulations promulgated by this Ministry in 2470. (7) Those who want to obtain a return-to-Siam passport should report to the county government and submit two photographs of themselves, seven centimeters long and six centimeters wide. After the county government is satisfied and approves, a passport will be issued. (8) If the police suspect that a person has no passport, they should notify the county government to summon that person for questioning. (9) This Ministry order will take effect on August 17th.

Cable Requesting Negotiations: The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce yesterday telegraphed the National Government's Executive Yuan, Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Ministry of Industry, and Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, saying, "We have just received a letter from the Siamese General Chamber of Commerce of China (see previous excerpts) regarding mutual respect, etc., and have attached a translation. We have learned that no fewer than 100,000 of our countrymen travel to and from Siam every year. If the regulations are implemented, it will cost each overseas Chinese at least 250 yuan in national currency to go to Siam each year. Other harsh regulations are not even being discussed. This expense alone is not something our overseas Chinese can afford. We hereby request that your esteemed departments and commissions investigate and approve our request to quickly find a way to negotiate the revocation or amendment of these regulations to protect overseas Chinese affairs. We are deeply praying and imploring. Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce of the Republic of China, Standing Committee Members Su Minsheng, Zhang Yuquan, Lu Guangji, Chen Riping, Li Kuian, Peng Chuli, et al., respectfully." (seal)

Establishment of the Chinese Pilots Association

Breaking a Decades-Long Monopoly by Foreigners

The First Sound of Reclaiming Pilotage Rights

For decades, the pilotage rights in various ports of our country have been occupied by foreigners. Previously, the Ministry of Finance, Navy, and Communications jointly proposed reclaiming these rights and having Chinese nationals take on these roles. Consequently, the Navy established a pilot training school in Shanghai to cultivate talent for succession. Following the labor strike by the foreign pilots association last month due to demands for increased fees, the Ministry of Finance, Navy, and Communications deemed it even more crucial to abolish foreign pilots. It has now been decided that an examination for pilot personnel will be held in Shanghai on October 1st to lay the groundwork for their employment. Chinese professionals in the maritime field have also quickly begun to establish the Chinese Pilots Association, setting up an office at 2 Ocean Creek Bridge on Avenue Edward VII. Preparations have been underway for several months, and now, with the examination date approaching, the association has officially announced its establishment. This is indeed the first sound of our country reclaiming its pilotage rights. Recognizing the significant impact of this matter on our national sovereignty, our reporter has diligently investigated and recorded the following information from various sources:

Election of Members　The Chinese Pilots Association is established by maritime professionals in Shanghai. The members include naval veterans and current shipowners, many of whom are highly experienced and knowledgeable maritime experts. Currently, the association members have elected Chen Ganqing as Chairman and He Hailan as Vice Chairman. Hao Dingxi, Liu Xun Da, Chen Jin Yu, and Huang Xiao Han have been selected as council members. The association will submit their resumes and constitution to the Navy for record.

Approval from the Navy　The association received a reply from the Navy yesterday, stating: "Your submission has been noted. Pilotage is related to national defense and is also subject to international law. This type of public-service nature should follow the established precedent of establishing associations for lawyers and accountants to ensure prudence. According to the report, the elected Chairman, Vice Chairman, and council members are either from maritime backgrounds or have long served on ships. Entrusting them with the affairs of the association should ensure a deep understanding of sovereignty. Approval is hereby granted. The submitted constitution has been slightly revised and is enclosed. Permission is granted for provisional implementation. Once the Examination Yuan issues pilot licenses and the administrative authority is determined, revisions and promulgation can be made if necessary. No other pilot associations have been established elsewhere, and your submission does not mention communication with any other association. The seal to be used should temporarily follow the style of the first type of seal stipulated in the regulations for professional groups. You may create and use the seal on your own." This is the reply.

Contents of the Constitution　The association's constitution consists of four chapters and twenty-one articles. Chapter One concerns the association, with Article One stating that individuals who have not obtained a license through examination by the Examination Yuan are not permitted to serve as pilots, nor are those who hold licenses but have not joined the Pilots Association. Article Two concerns the pilotage area. Articles Four through Nine concern the organization of the association, including the holding of meetings and the election of the chairman. Chapter Two, on responsibilities, Articles Ten through Fifteen, specifies that pilots who neglect their duties and cause damage to ships shall be held responsible. All military secrets regarding military ports, fortresses, and military affairs must not be divulged. Pilot licenses must not be used fraudulently, and official commissions from government agencies must not be declined. Articles Sixteen through Eighteen comprise Chapter Three on disciplinary measures. Violations of this chapter and the association's rules will result in penalties ranging from admonishment, suspension from duty for two months to one year, or revocation of the license. Those whose licenses are revoked cannot reapply to be a pilot for two years. Individuals subjected to disciplinary action may request a review from the competent authority through the Pilots Association, but only once. Articles Nineteen to Twenty-one comprise Chapter Four on obligations. Pilots must report any illegal activities discovered on ships to the competent authority and convene a meeting to review and present the facts and reasons. Pilots, commissioned by judicial authorities, will review the causes of shipwrecks within their pilotage area and serve as appraisers. (Due to the length of the original text, the above is a summarized account.)

Seeking a Way Forward　Following the establishment of the association, it should actively promote pilotage services, aiming to gradually have the association's personnel guide all Chinese and foreign merchant ships in and out of ports, so that foreign pilots will withdraw completely. The Navy has agreed to lend the association a pilot boat to assist in its operations. However, given the deeply entrenched foreign influence in Shanghai and the special relationship between foreign merchant ships and foreign pilots, it will not be easy for the Chinese Pilots Association to secure the pilotage of foreign merchant ships. All of this requires the assistance of the central government with political power so that Chinese pilotage can rise in time and replace foreign pilots. The association is preparing to submit a request to various ministries for concrete assistance in the association's future endeavors.

Suspect Arrested for Falsely Requesting Expansion of the Concession

Wang Axing of West Shanghai

Under Detention by the Public Security Bureau

According to the National News Agency, after the "Ta Mei Wan Bao" (Shanghai Evening Post) published a report that 200,000 merchants and residents of West Shanghai had requested the expansion of the concession by the Public Works Department (PWD), the Municipal Public Security Bureau (MPSB) launched a rigorous investigation to determine the truth. It has now been learned that Wang Axing, a known hooligan from Zhoujiaqiao, is the prime suspect, and he was arrested yesterday on a warrant. Wang Axing has long been a notorious pest in West Shanghai, also known as Xingshan, nicknamed Xinxin, and nicknamed Rotten-Head Ali. Originally from a poor family in Gaojiagang, Zhoujiaqiao township, he lost his parents at a young age and associated with local thugs from childhood. In the Zhoujiaqiao and Caojiadu areas, he engaged in extortion and blackmail, acting in a brutal and overbearing manner, feared by residents like a tiger. Later, he maneuvered to obtain the position of local security officer, becoming even more unscrupulous. He often colluded with foreign merchants and engaged in acts of currying favor with foreigners. He opened a teahouse to gather gamblers and recruit thugs, thus expanding his influence, much to the suffering of the residents. After receiving a report that Wang Axing was suspected of falsely representing West Shanghai merchants and requesting the PWD to expand the concession, the Municipal Public Security Bureau secretly dispatched Inspector Cao from the Inspection Department, along with the chief of the Zhoujiaqiao police station in the 6th District, to arrest him at the Hongjinyuan teahouse and Yuanxiang general store that Wang Axing ran, at one o'clock in the afternoon of the day before yesterday. Upon arrival, Wang Axing was out, so they told the store staff, "The police chief wants to talk to him. Please ask him to come to the police station as soon as possible." Meanwhile, several plainclothes policemen were dispatched to guard the vicinity. At around 6 o'clock, Wang Axing returned to the store. Upon hearing the report from the store staff, he thought the police chief had something else to discuss, so he went to the Zhoujiaqiao police station with his head held high. Unexpectedly, the arresting officers were waiting. As soon as he was seen, he was handcuffed and taken away. Wang Axing vehemently protested his innocence and requested Inspector Cao not to arrest him today, but to wait until tomorrow for him to turn himself in for questioning. Inspector Cao refused. Seeing this situation, Wang Axing could not escape, so he requested to go to the store to change clothes so he could accompany them. The Inspector agreed. Wang Axing entered the store and went upstairs to change, finally coming down after a long time. He was then escorted into the waiting car. After getting in, Wang Axing took out a hundred-dollar bill and secretly handed it to Inspector Cao, asking for help. Inspector Cao pretended to agree and put it in his pocket. Upon reaching the Public Security Bureau, he presented Wang Axing and the bribe of one hundred dollars to the authorities for prosecution. It is reported that the authorities consider the case to be of great importance and have decided to conduct a rigorous interrogation.

Opposition to Surety Deposits for Taxes

Taxpayers Association Requests the Public Works Department to Abolish the Practice

The Shanghai Concession Chinese Taxpayers Association sent a letter to the Director-General of the Shanghai Municipal Council yesterday, stating: "Dear Sir, according to a letter from Zhang Zhenxin Sauce Garden, regarding their Yuhe Zhenji Sauce Shop, located at No. 111 Xiangkang Lane, Meibaige Road, Shanghai International Settlement, which opened on August 25th. As per usual, they applied to the Revenue Office of the Shanghai Municipal Council for a liquor license in advance. After an investigation and estimation by the office, the quarterly tax was assessed at twelve taels of silver. Now, according to the new regulations, a surety deposit of thirty taels of silver is also required. The shop's staff argued that there was no such precedent and refused to pay. However, the office insisted on the payment. After several disputes, they were unsuccessful. At that time, due to the urgency of the opening and the many tasks involved, they had no choice but to pay the surety deposit of thirty taels of silver and the half-season autumn liquor tax of six taels to obtain the license. Taxes are different from electricity and telephone services and should not require surety deposits. Therefore, we respectfully submit this letter to your council to protest to the Public Works Department, requesting that the surety deposit requirement be abolished to ease the burden and comply with legal principles. We eagerly await your response." Upon investigation, the requirement of surety deposits for taxes is unprecedented in the world. Therefore, we respectfully request that you investigate the matter and promptly abolish the surety deposit requirement and return the deposits already collected to their original owners.

China's First Self-Made Car

Now on Display at the Road and City Exhibition

China's first automobile is the Minsheng heavy-duty truck manufactured by Li Yichun, the director of the Liaoning Mortar Factory. The Minsheng Factory is attached to the Mortar Factory. It has been specially praised by Vice Commander Zhang and a huge amount of funds have been allocated. The heavy-duty truck has a load capacity of two tons and is best suited for modern Chinese roads. The size is similar to that of a general imported two-ton truck. Regarding the manufacturing method, except for the engine, electrical instruments, meters, and tires, which are temporarily specialized products, all other parts are designed and manufactured in-house. The durability and strength are particularly superior to those of ordinary heavy-duty trucks, while the price is lower. The characteristics are extracted as left.

The water tank is divided into four parts. Ordinary ruts. Water tanks are generally only one. If damaged, they cannot move. The Minsheng heavy-duty truck is divided into four parts. If one part is damaged, it can still operate as usual. Even if it needs to be repaired, the cost is relatively low.

The leaf spring is strong. The front and rear leaf springs are semi-elliptical. Manufactured from chrome vanadium steel. Both ends of the axle holes have special bronze bushings. The thickness is one-quarter thicker than other vehicles. It is naturally superior.

Can swing. If the tire is tilted into the mud in low-lying areas, the car body can swing. The car body can immediately drive out of the mud.

Climbing is unique. If you encounter a slope or a high place, the car will not be affected when driving at 25 or 35 degrees. It's like walking on flat ground. It can be stopped momentarily in the middle of the hillside. You can still muster strength to move forward. There is no risk of pouring backwards.

As described above. We are very fortunate that China has an amazing industrial product. In the future, the factory's efforts and progress will benefit the national industry and commerce and recover countless outflows of profits. The Six Major Features of the Shunfeng Brand New Car

—Fu

Has Natural Buoyancy and Free Eat-Row - sensationalized the entire lowest-priced car industry

The Shunfeng brand new car with natural buoyancy and free-row. Since it was announced to the world by Mr. Chrysler, it has been rumored everywhere. The reputation has risen. The Maddie Automobile Company in this city has now arrived in large quantities. The various styles will be on public display starting Saturday the 12th of this month. It is what the Shunfeng brand engineer calls natural buoyancy. Because of this feature, the entire prime mover machine can float naturally on its natural axis.

Chrysler and Shunfeng brand automobile company engineers all believe that the contribution of natural buoyancy to automobile construction is very significant and most valuable. In addition to automatic starting machines, four-wheel racing cars, and steel cars. This should be the fourth major success in automotive engineering. After a long period of measurement and test ride, it has been definitively proven that the function of natural buoyancy can definitely open a new era for four-cylinder cars. The vibration of the four-cylinder engine has been completely eliminated. The economy of a four-cylinder car and the stability of an eight-cylinder car are combined into one. This is something that has never happened before. It is really rare and valuable.

In the past, automobile engineering experts have exhausted all efforts to avoid the vibration and simplicity of four-cylinder engines. By the time the number of cylinders increased, the automobile industry was dedicated to the research and improvement of six-cylinder and eight-cylinder models. They no longer paid attention to four-cylinder engines. However, the engineers of Shunfeng brand continue to work hard and never slacken. Compared with any vehicle with the same machine power performance, it is equal. There is no difference. Therefore, except for the only drawback of vibration, the four-cylinder car is worthy of being the most complete of the lowest-priced vehicles.

However, the vibration of the four-cylinder car is no longer a worry now. Since Mr. Sanders, deputy director of the engineering department of Chrysler Corporation, first created and successfully announced natural buoyancy, the only shortcoming of engine vibration is that the entire prime mover is floating inside the chassis. It is possible to dissipate the car body frame without leaving any residue. The avoidance of engine vibration has a great relationship with the rubber absorption. The floating power invented and successfully developed by Shunfeng brand engineers is the use of new rubber devices. For example, two engine rubber frames are used instead of the usual three or four. However, the position of these two frames is just right. Fit the scientific principle. Therefore, floating power can achieve this unprecedented great effect. The rear rubber frame is installed in the transverse gear after the power transmission machine. The front frame is just installed under the water pump and supported by a special triangular arc attached to the front transverse gear. The line connecting the front and rear frames must pass through the center of gravity of the prime mover machine. Therefore, the entire prime mover machine is supported by absolute average. In order to maintain the engine's proper straight line and make its action fit within the range allowed by the rubber frame,

There is no need for lubrication. There is no risk of joint loosening. Lever fragmentation. And cable expansion. Strict protection. Rain and snow do not invade. Its sensitive and accurate actions are even more outstanding. Unreachable.

The above six major features. What other vehicles are there? There is no one who can combine them. However, the Shunfeng brand new car. In addition to having both. There are also many other advantages. Such as the beauty of the lines. Harmony of colors. Exquisite equipment and decoration. The spectacular new-style water tank and water tank cap. In order to ensure that all major and minor parts of mechanical engineering are excellent and outstanding. Numerous. It is hard to count. The reason why Shunfeng brand new cars are perfect and sensationalize the entire lowest-priced car industry. It is because of this.

After Visiting the Road and City Exhibition

— Zhizheng

Inspiring the Nation's Interest in Road Building, Reducing Various Obstacles to Road Building, and Pioneering the Production of Homemade Automobiles

The grand and vibrant National Road and City Exhibition has opened amidst cheers from the masses. Although the scale of this exhibition is not particularly large, generally speaking, the achievement of collecting and exhibiting the road conditions of the entire country within a short period of preparation is already commendable. I believe that although the duration of this exhibition is not long, it has left a particularly deep impression on the people of the country. Road-building movements have long been in full swing in the United States, while in our country, this is only the first time that this topic has been raised. Naturally, it is a matter worthy of celebration.

In the past decade, natural and man-made disasters have followed one after another. Recently, floods have spread across more than ten provinces, with cries of grief heard everywhere and a scene too tragic to bear. Of course, natural disasters cannot be prevented by human power. However, if the country had excellent roads, then when one area suffers from floods, another area could immediately use automobiles to provide relief, transporting food from morning till night. At the same time, the disaster-stricken people could also be immediately transported to a safe area. Whenever China encounters famine, it is at a loss for what to do, and watches the people die without being able to provide relief, simply because of the lack of roads. Therefore, from the perspective of providing disaster relief, road construction is urgently needed. This is the first point. In addition to natural disasters, there are also man-made disasters. In recent years, bandits have been lurking and harassing everywhere, taking advantage of the inconvenient transportation, leaving the government troops helpless. It is difficult to advance and suppress them, and the bandit forces are becoming more and more rampant. If there is a good network of roads connecting all parts of the country, then naturally the bandit disasters can be suppressed without a fight. This is the second point. In recent years, there has been a high call to "go to the frontier" because the population in the interior is too large and life is difficult. The frontier is vast and sparsely populated, making it easier to make a living. Therefore, everyone hopes to send a portion of the people to the frontier for reclamation. However, reclamation cannot be achieved with empty words. At present, the transportation between our country's frontier and the interior can be said to be extremely isolated. To go to Yunnan, one must pass through Annam to be fast. To go to Xinjiang takes several dozen days. Recently, Red Russia built three railways connecting to the vicinity of Xinjiang from Moscow, taking only eight days. As a result, although everyone is willing to go, there is no road to take. The so-called rich resources of the frontier can only be seized by others. If there are good roads, then automobiles can reach directly, providing great convenience. People will naturally be happy to go, and the effect of reclamation can be achieved without encouragement. This is the third point. Related to the reclamation of the frontier is also the consolidation of national defense. The Chinese government has inconvenient transportation with the frontier, and in political terms, it is beyond its reach. Those fertile lands can only be allowed to be plundered. Looking at the history of various countries, those who have lost their countries often start with transportation. Germany is a militarist democratic country. Before the European War, it had already set up railway lines on the border. Later, when the war began, the German army moved to the Western Front when it was not very tense on the Eastern Front, and returned to the Eastern Front when the Western Front was relaxed, going back and forth with great convenience. Therefore, one team of men could be used as two teams. The value of transportation in military affairs is not difficult to imagine. Today, China is facing foreign aggression, and the frontiers should not be left wide open. If railways are difficult to build, roads must not be delayed. This is the fourth point. The knowledge of the Chinese people is only more developed in large cities, while the interior is still mostly very backward. This is naturally also the influence of inconvenient transportation. Because of inconvenient transportation, it is difficult for people to travel. They are stuck in one place, culture cannot be instilled, and knowledge cannot be developed. To carry out self-governance during the period of political tutelage, there must be sound civic education. From this perspective, roads are of utmost importance. This is the fifth point. Therefore, from the above five points, China's need for roads can be said to be extremely urgent. The Road Association is holding a road and city exhibition at this time, which is really the only stimulant for the people. (To be continued)

News

Selection of the Tongyu Route (Continued)

— Shanlang

(3) Comparison with the Yelanba Line: This line still goes from Yingzuiyan, through Shuikouba, Gouzimen, up to Taiba, the Erdunyan and Mei'ya on the side of Yelan, and the Jiantou'ya to Yanyan. It then reaches Ganshui via the Xiaojiupan in Sichuan. The route is slightly longer than the Xin-Song line, and the terrain rises and falls, with few flat routes. The slopes in places such as Gouzimen, Mei'ya, and Jiantou'ya are very steep, and the twists and turns are even greater. Moreover, there are few towns along the way, with only Yelan. Also, because the terrain is low, it cannot pass through the market but only passes through the Erdunyan on the mountainside. Therefore, the area through which this line passes not only has poor routes and large projects, but it is also desolate and has no prosperous markets compared to the Xin-Song route.

(4) Comparison with the Yangcungou and Xin-Song Riverside Line: This line goes from Maliu, through Yangcun, Lucun, Anhe, Huaqiudang, to Xinzhan. Then it follows the Xin-Song River channel, through Lianghekou and Diaoyudong, to Ganshui. The upper section of the route is located in the two-story valley behind the Shiniulan slope. Although there is a lot of cultivated land, there are overlapping gullies and excessive slopes. If the route is lowered, it will deviate to the side, and if it is raised, it will be all exposed rocks. Moreover, the Anhe River floods easily, submerging the valley and cutting off traffic. Huaqiudang is parallel to Xinzhan, and the mountain is more than 800 meters high. A lightning-shaped route of at least thirty miles is needed to reach the foot of the mountain, and it is mostly rocky, requiring huge engineering work. It is more than twenty miles longer than the first line. Therefore, this section of the route is not possible. From Xinzhan onwards, the route goes out along the river, through Songkan, Lianghekou, and Diaoyudong to Ganshui. Although the route is flat, there are many places where cliffs are opposite each other. For example, in the section from Mengdu to Chenghuangmiao, there are several cliffs. The twenty miles from Lianghekou to Diaoyudong is entirely steep cliffs. It is difficult even for railways to pass, and it is even more difficult for roads to pass. It is not as easy to build as the first line. Therefore, neither the upper nor lower sections are possible.

(5) Comparison of Partial Sections of the Xin-Song Line: (1) Tongguyuan Line: This line is a comparison line between Liangfengya and Shanpo. It goes straight down from Liangfengya along the ditch, through Tongguyuan and Hedu, to Shanpo. The route is more direct, but in the section from Liangfengya straight down to the ditch, there are more than ten lightning-shaped turns, with excessive twists and turns. The route is poor. There are large rocks along both ends of Hedu, and it is also next to the river. The work of blasting rocks and building embankments is quite large. It is not as flat and labor-saving as the Huaqiuping line. (2) Shiniulan Line: This line is another comparison line between Chumipu and Shanpo. It goes from Chumipu along the original road through Yaquewo, Zushiguan, Shiniulan to Mentouqing. Then it slopes down from the mountainside through Wayao ping to Shanpo, about forty miles long. Most of the entire route is rocky mountains, and there are many cliffs and deep valleys, making construction even more difficult. Moreover, the slopes in the Yaquewo and Zushiguan areas are slightly larger. The route here cannot pass without many lightning-shaped turns. Therefore, this line is not only a huge project, but the route is also poor, far inferior to the flat and labor-saving earth hills in the opposite Huaqiuping area. (3) Wangjiafen Line:

This line is a comparison line between Qizhenxi and Sangyuanba. It slopes up from Qizhenxi, through Hehuaping, to Wangjiafen, and then slopes down to Sangyuanba. This line was selected to avoid the tens of feet of large rocks at Chenghuang Temple. Although there is a lot of soil quality in the entire section, there are also occasional rocky mountains. From Wangjiafen onwards, it is all rock. In total, the rock embankment work in this section is almost equal to the rock embankment project at Chenghuang Temple. Moreover, the upper and lower sections of Qizhenxi and Wangjiafen both need to use lightning shapes. It is not as flat and direct as going along the river from Chenghuang Temple and blasting rocks to pass through. Although the rocks at Chenghuang Temple are large, they are no more than eighty feet long. The river surface in the lower half is wide, and the water level, even during the spring and summer floods, is no more than a few feet high. The roadbed in this half can be completely built by building embankments in the river, without blasting rocks. Only the upper half is steep and the road position is high. The river bottom is deep and the impact force is large, making it difficult to build embankments and requiring complete rock blasting. However, the rock is only forty feet long, and the cost is only a few thousand yuan. After careful consideration, it is better than the Hehuaping Wangjiafen line. One cannot sacrifice this good route because of minor difficulties. (4) Xiematai Line: This line is a comparison line between Songkan and Jiudianya. It slopes up from the Koukou field in Songkan along the left side of the mountain to Nongwan, Xiematai, Tianbasha Wangmiao, and reaches Jiudianya. It is thirty miles long, more than ten miles longer than the Bazhuaxi line. Although there are fewer exposed rocks, it seems easier to work on. However, after a few inches of topsoil, the interior and exterior of the soil are still rocks. In total, the rock embankment work on this thirty-mile section is only more than the exposed rock work on the few miles of Bazhuaxi. Moreover, the Tianba section of Xiematai is a valley with excessive slopes. There are also at least ten lightning-shaped routes. It is not as direct, labor-saving, and less winding than the Bazhuaxi line. Therefore, it was originally planned to use the Xiematai line. After detailed review, the Bazhuaxi line is still better. The Bazhuaxi line is an excellent road line from Songkan to Sichuan. Although the rocks are slightly larger and the cost is slightly higher, it is only necessary to blast a foot-wide rock inward and build a few-foot embankment outward to complete the construction of the roadbed. Once this type of rocky mountain route is completed, it can reduce maintenance work.

In summary, all routes should be from Xin-Song for the sake of reducing engineering work for the people. The government should also be from Xin-Song for the sake of saving expenses. For the convenience of transportation and the development of towns along the way, it should also be from Xin-Song. Therefore, the colleagues of this team spared no effort to traverse the rugged paths and overcome dangers. After many comparisons, they were able to select this route. Although they dare not say that it is a good route, there is no other route better than this one. Therefore, for this selection of the Xin-Song route, the Chongqing survey comrades expressed their sympathy after the joint survey and gave up the proposal of using Wenshui as the intersection point. It is certainly not that the surveyors have any bias or error in the selection. (End)
